Programmatic, Indoors And Out

 

Automation isn't just for websites anymore. The WSJ's Suzanne Vranica focuses on how programmatic tools are being used for radio and out-of-home buying, which are among the oldest traditional media formats. "We are always looking for ways to make it simpler to put together an out-of-home campaign," said Clear Channel CEO William Eccleshare. Read the rest <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001aQRcLaNt3HZAseeFD4qnOaGVU9LIe_FXaYJLjcwvzgtqPGhapTBSRyTHaCOc5OzZIFLO332bxThBlxl4MLr1pGl06gDxTJWPx_PJTsxPGPFG6AlMkOIV9QD8G_XDxOkX_PYMDr8B_BgYUvsc7Fa8vB4wkNnrWaKMts33d3v_JAaM4sZ9kklnRKruQnm7n4Jd> .

 

Salesforce.com Trumps SAP

 

Salesforce.com has grabbed the title of largest worldwide CRM away from SAP, according to a new report from Gartner. The research firm also noted total CRM software revenue rose 12.5% to $18 billion from last year. "Competition among CRM software vendors really heated up in 2012, as major players continued to vie for broader market penetration internationally and more widespread adoption within midsize to large enterprises," said Joanne Correia, vice president at Gartner, in a statement. Read the release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001aQRcLaNt3HZZTuVxcf4YjlHFcrjfL_y1CA8llAJRQuqxJ5yq-Zw4s6JgelMklypWPty_YoC56BTGlp4qfadEVHOAaQe0xnaUucBZYC5-9Xgj1D0vFR4qHXZ0nTOS--6rnIvqnW85U3ndVx5siabsKw==> 

 

18,000%

 

Now, there's a growth figure your favorite state lottery would be proud of: 18,000%. According to a press release, that's the amount of revenue growth for publishers that sell-side platform PubMatic has seen in its private marketplace/exchange product line. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001aQRcLaNt3HZslkyGD3uHxFB-A1MXeAHSv5G41dSudRIGAaBhArzDZ2nMLanrmmJMmlwCseuWaParhk0g6ppg3RgcS7xkchJ1h_8jfSzoOVmw8eZeSC9R5_tiTjoc2fhzxKj9fWqdvakoAVBvJcAnZA-_qY8Z_7nQc_zGx9Ui7GZlm4A4Nizd1LnQRvvG7RyKGyP2nhciiyWFSfU9-262MG_TJ0N6YXVjnyriL8dLwptbewcGy4NrSUMaVl1rCvMdOJq-G4bmvkWGNSvaYtG35VdbmD4pXEuVElzo8V_NVYteNr39v94em9raAXIE28eiupBZ36nyrtg=> .

 

Lean Marketing

 

Marketers can benefit from testing their campaigns on a smaller scale using real-time bidding (RTB) before allocating huge budgets to them. Ratko Vidakovic, Director of Marketing at SiteScout, outlines four phases to getting the most out of a campaign: building, analyzing, optimizing and scaling. Vidakovic adds, "Knowing the inherent volatility in RTB volumes, approaching publishers for direct buys (after testing, of course) only makes sense." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001aQRcLaNt3HYZ0i1CyTbAWUgTVtXArYzUUQMfJt2dKD8JZKHKsXVCXCCrZwvZ_Ecu8vMDSTKdv50aMAiCiDBGKN_lUGZGfyXUoe_g_O8rn8aGbu-JDkkKAZHTaRnuSqPbQT5IXXcghBsEJ0aIL-MU9tlQO9V9g7sbHu7sje7WqdSzrDxNDwZs7JzaPyt4V9x0> 

 

RTB-Naysayer Gets Creative

 

Jim Bankoff, CEO of publisher Vox Media, took the stage at TechCrunch's Disrupt conference, reiterating his aversion to real-time bidding as a "race to the bottom" that his company would continue to resist <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001aQRcLaNt3HY5vEKGvGTjIiFun82lOd5sPQYOelFH1OnTssGYRsuKhK6U-IFnQBcyvbc9mViPE4GQT_22db58ElPU4Qc50SOYsJTTMYiekRvJ1EhcnFxQRdElWSDNILRKGAd-TzAf-okImwjgqhQLlzVyOdbxhqDnz7fcBHTtxtyAwI8LDLKrhKZ8kVkG3C8x7nHHom-kLbTa-Xls88zmke0qf4v6zJ7bUWayA6KoAN-cIe5jSHQj9JwrhqsfVTzu>  in favor of direct sales. Moreover, the publisher will be adding an in-house marketing shop dubbed Vox Creative, which would create blogs for sponsors. According to TechCrunch, Bankoff said, "You see ugly advertising...but we think there is a great market to be cracked in premium, high-quality ads." Read the rest <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001aQRcLaNt3HZfdIP7KYyROFuzImWYPbABk4WgElI4Q3hJ6WKtwXzALlxgt6qHeBeA2w0pg5VaseSlDxeoeULuL-KrIGPhSps6I0OPng7g_S9mwts4Q2-hj5zCEeQrdR9bCURQz-IMIAYhzeUY6xlDQaWhT-y4ODLe1vQ62h0LNM853x6U0vVVKlTW0s9b4GAfr70V4UF_8Vq4F2hqQEx27jfo2z1UEPlxG00WGIYyRo7jXzZbd3h7zcSLlO1k_X6Slfs_j-He7tG72Cl3U7StzOQ06eisKWPspW80nRP5OfNfJWUj_1H9_CNqjm7E3IWFC_0_RBIv_8zFB16Gvs9AjG929nNWQNwIvym7XQZGqDBMX9iaBF7lzzue004SElIUMQypHsDzp3WAzSpL5_xGuLIEeOJGsQG4> .

Hot Ecommerce

 

Japan-based ecommerce marketplace Rakuten (formerly Buy.com) is breaking into the US market with a focus on shopping experiences rather than just utility. "We come at ecommerce with a very different concept. It is about how to empower small- to medium-sized merchants using the internet rather than competing against them and trying to destroy them," said CEO and cofounder Hiroshi Mikitani. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001aQRcLaNt3HboAgjqN1PL4LSt0oavI0VlddD0Fc7M-1FMqUkOFOa55-YhNLaw9R8NDAknFeaNZ358hP0jjoy-LrDAB6bSoGehDMx-d1H6oj77dQHOxv0nOaKx1AyCKJ6l7BP16U1aJrW1D0LXHQELJg-B9x7N7tFmKHcmzVbmdGI=>  Its LinkShare Rakuten division bought retargeter MediaForge in September 2012 <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001aQRcLaNt3HabrQu98NS5vIax8R4yiZa3YNccOWZRrxgsM49Bdft3mrhvcj1I7E8z72fKPRHUembo1fcFWhHlcmsCgH_UiTaIygdUVNvas9EIM2d_S1x0wC8s5g-1P_yLk2WHKwXv8GnVMod-o_C8uPvnqV-aaxIxHKs_ZK4MjHo=> .

 

Measuring Viral Bennies

 

While video analytics specialist Visible Measures doesn't promise the ability to make a viral video, its partnership with Publicis Groupe's VivaKi does try to quantify the value of a viral video with Contagion, an earned media measurement tool. "Our agencies can [use Contagion to] change campaign variables like the budget commitment, offline and online channel mix, site list, and more, and determine how these changes will affect overall campaign performance," said Kate Sirkin, Publicis SMG's global research director. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001aQRcLaNt3HYRUYKQdkq3Mkc_NE4Y_xW_StGgRguaMkVx8GFQHtTKlH8bNpHbN8yItzaJ1MUgeiBdgFXJmuqrg_WrfAlrytC8W60zG9Q6pebtvcXeSRd3Bvvhjv74B_D5KLYo2INpnRXWiuEeQQuJe9f7vW3O4U0mQhfRMc2SF31HgIqzOQ7lXGj0W9dWVUGtTCBZwAbkCBE7HzIqv4kpkKoCCgruXA8ugA6qRvRCXzd9zWS35NawdEau8N96c-ptQloy3X8P-D8=> .

 

Maximizing Digital Video Potential

 

There is a huge opportunity to capture the 45 million viewers of original professional online video <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001aQRcLaNt3HYxLt5-qPV0yNqrnZiMIp5hkW8uqkzkacwdhVJ0fDzeP18Wb75Mm42KL9NUWNKnB9DC_7YnHmC-kt_lrrimTNWTtyr9mmcpSJpxqK80tovF6BLS38Qbw7zPaWFmQZOlKUhPQeWbz02rAT8VtbT5Cs0mcJLVeeBYTlA3zCg7b7brGx-gjMK_j5pJnwHWgHOFBteXKmXjVo4QFDeEia2YS6GLzehTjI9ebUibLqlbm1H38g==>  by using more interactive and robust ads, says the IAB's Randall Rothenberg in an Adweek think piece. Rothenberg points out that the most popular digital video ad is a 30-minute video for Invisible Children, which garnered over 97 million views, perhaps proving viewers crave a deeper ad video experience. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001aQRcLaNt3HZ4oxxiSRX4YTRj0P7xz8RbvYqWggcBr9hxWllo7alJhx7TcbKHRlKN3o4z8zeLh1mJhG88BCEfkTvrIxQmJysj1qwvP9Kl5matLH6pTJtPPPFXnE_1hAeaZ7ed3neZOaptEWTjG0-6JaCjclCm23DOmH7tUafQRc_cP-FQsleQaKDyglzpkNvheIsf_T3xT7mY1OYndASAvRG7n9AQ-xjx> 

 

Hyperlocal RTB

 

Publishers have a potential opportunity to reap the benefits of RTB through local and hyperlocal geo-targeting, according to Dick O'Hare. By representing a very specific location, these publishers have an advantage over the somewhat unreliable method of IP-based geo-targeting. "In this rapidly evolving world, publishers become relegated to a supply of cookies for marketers to target versus an audience targetable through the association of the publisher's content and audience profiles," O'Hare says. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001aQRcLaNt3HbAMUcLpp3MzCS-mUXTcCICpQkNVSn7yLjEjopuKak9RG7szRU-fyjt_E6DU2xoiuIvuKSE_dqTjZ2jB1rMtLJVKGIb95R2y1wKBjJ3O5bsJ1pSnsepXSRKwtarI4vtoGfZQSV0wbIgBZ9liqqFkWcBsSqwq3X5GaJ6UcrN6f2XMHdoiyYViKB8meWbHGq7cPQM954XRQNi2AEWH_d4OBXTzQc5-SMZ7Bo=> 

 

Frequency Capping

 

The idea of frequency capping is simple enough - make sure users aren't inundated with the same ad over and over across a series of sites - but agencies and publishers can't (or, in worst cases, won't) institute effective caps, according to a whitepaper by Michael Green, Audience Science's director of research and marketing strategy. In a relatively small study of what the researcher called "six typical campaigns run in Q4 2012 by large national advertisers," Audience Science found that "out-of-frequency impressions are not only common, they're the norm. No campaign delivered more than 40% of its impressions within the frequency cap, and one campaign saw over 3/4ths of its impressions exceed the cap." Download the whitepaper here <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001aQRcLaNt3HZW9-VE71m03PtDAQYktbD8rykYgpKH5ZmB1etvl6yU8AOip8J5b6GBHhrvaAF4i700_i07aXvvD9hfVb-vy37qTq_q8UjYQgp11kNRYqCsEBVR4-hc4Ht-FP0JzJ-QvtSa5baHNpBBE8T1zHKX_tnJ4hyGcOvmZYo=> .

 

Big Ads! - Native, Too

 

Yahoo announced at its NewFront presentation that it was adding a big old billboard ad on its home page as well as native advertising its calling "stream ads" - stories within Yahoo's stream of content. Anthony Ha at TechCrunch writes, "When I asked how the new ads will affect the consumer experience, [VP of Product and Media Mike Kerns] didn't say specifically, but he did note that's something Yahoo will be tracking - specifically how the ads affect the consumer engagement numbers on its properties." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001aQRcLaNt3Ha_BXyyz_JTG7iLPuCROqzSkxFc_W_N2rKTLyx1W8uYsON9WU22AdR3X9KKcMbSvSmGwPSiMIB0RcuBc8GZ-hOxM5-NxcTaU67hO__ocoNrKm5oLap6QCJib98BREwY3BR_b1arqMpL24R55wg9uVvK>

Cheaper, Future Inventory

 

YouTube says its an "upfront" contrarian and is lowering rates for media buyers in a bid to attract a bigger share of those TV budgets. "Last year we were rigid; we got a few big advertisers with huge checks," YouTube sales chief Lucas Watson tells AdAge's Michael Learmonth. "We got a lot of feedback about being inflexible so now we are breaking them down into more manageable chunks." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001hyeiuOBT_R1TSi17tUvRBeV6H1MGnAmi4K60NoXzjIgZGQ45TbFa5A7jCh7jOzvJuBE6e9Gcwz9K_gXrZtuEsDb-NSL0rQqtuKw-IxPdJuIU4cnm5sszf_XgxNMsvStEDPX7HU0E0POH_FDUdhF-lpmVgKQMBmB5CUfqntE0GvRkEe7MaaFfn7eYYVERXMhlO16rZ6OaV5KZ3EF_LhqL2g==> .

 

More Yahoo Turmoil?

 

Yahoo Chairman Fred Amoroso announcing on Friday that he would not seek another term after only a year in the post has observers wondering if a clear direction for the portal is still a work-in-progress. In his official statement, Amoroso suggests that he's stepping down according to his previous plan and expressed security in Mayer at the helm, adding, "this is a natural time for me to transition off the board, consistent with what I said a year ago." Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001hyeiuOBT_R2iTa8h0terSx1JJrX0nh6W8PsfBl9d4_NWQAVrdMxC9pi8whzI6PowWjY4hxweNVBB7u8rK9xg8w4JPtuiQD8uXNCyCfZA2DBunn9IgaH_-loNaDY8z-PYq_5IQj3-lfzrnTtX_4-pKYdapDhjAL1zfu0U5j0ZFdmy4_L9pBmpHg==> .

 

Marketing The Trends

 

On his personal blog, VivaKi's Rishad Tobaccowala outlines "Six Current and Six Rapidly Expanding Trends Marketers Should Focus On" that was also offered at the recent Publicis Investor Conference. Coming in at #5: "The future will be about more access and less ownership - Consumers increasingly want access to content (Spotify, Netflix etc.) or things (Zip car etc.) rather than just ownership. This will also be true in the world of big data." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001hyeiuOBT_R32AorO6JAwXirTA4Dz9831kvVugnZOnawYz2K6kDKgPo5WgdGl7dU-QFH-a8doKcb3CC70zO6o3wgdx_nwbyY4roQpohJC9s8Lqz6lXA8wYSNQEy72vNvujHAxhFwbvKjldJZESna8QZcxkM809t9GFCiQ0DRNYXvRR4TBtfnebhwudXhCj8j4WErti4PUuwCFWpaS3HulyMP3zLgkKU0USrA9AfLnOflW0F17UKTUUA==> . Meanwhile, Publicis VIvaKi's agency trading desk offering Audience On Demand has created a new video explaining what it does for clients. See it now on VivaKi-er Marco Bertozzi's blog. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001hyeiuOBT_R3Ufc5dBK52xFuEwJ5PInmB1W1KtI5YZtGLch_a2VPiI_Xl1ls2y_YUBOmIsyjbBGq-Ooy-eCzOlDKWqzc_gpMuljN-mKf2zHyMnjTJRbwGpbVLFjeSJsWHT_7s2LAc0NZ9sgr5IpwdUk0LnVn1IsOh-2bSa3Qn2gGx_sXZI-TBIxpxVr30smoH8pokPVQ92ng6WGM4kXGJ5w==> 

 

Video Ad Guarantee

 

Jun Group has tapped the "money-back guarantee" in an effort to track new video advertisers to its ad network. Adweek's Mike Shields reports, "Jun is promising buyers that it won't deliver any pop under ads, autoplay videos, bogus views or ads on undesirable places (like say, ghost sites)." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001hyeiuOBT_R1ybk5DBD6AtlXjiDDdd7iNelI76Q07kauPkneXahfqb6Cy47irB0z7-aLlONsMmhQVcsuj2U4tPKeOIwbjw7UlHp68g0mmnssRtSeNJP758X9Lz0t8yptNRcjy2ASgF6rFvGzdZMEQtc227E7zwvdSsGtBpM7ZbJkVLetlc97CCiTlNdNF1rm7I7Hu4nXD8gxCEXObZZkT7xyPedX2ZT7t>  Also, read AdExchanger's Oct. '12 Q <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001hyeiuOBT_R3B0rayZSh0aHUpffKQG8xKBQ8djBmHjLmZHvS4yn70irbwC1Fb7nSB_rfZUtugOICeWZ2LObqZPxaf6qO65mI7GRth_F1mJeAbJrIzGX2Mb6juOO1ShjYK9qY1wxU1isFXji494if-XLAWKKit-QJJnGeq_G7Wh9PloQWN9kMaEFF426331hpCK65mNMrj5x0LcEBgY0QOnNv7kkffrTJnifnof3BmyY3acvqutZeL23412gr0NdCn> &A with Jun CEO Mitchell Reichgut.

 

Whither The Audience

 

On Digiday, Jack Marshall says that ad buyers are frustrated with certain publisher audience development tactics. He notes, for example, Complex.com's SEO for porn-related terms. Marshall paraphrases Complex CEO Rich Antoniello who explains that "less than 6 percent of the publisher's traffic now comes from searches related to the word 'porn' and that it's not focusing on SEO to build audience. Rather, Antoniello said, it's been investing heavily in editorial staff..." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001hyeiuOBT_R1tqDmcvsvecx1wfQUpyzQAgwfdSABjVrZKO9dPHoXYsqEkoeF_6H2hpEcj_Muh1My28juoc7ziOqWh2MGZTNN9IEUpsnKX-82cZ2Yd3GUBS1urU9uqzSSMy0f64jaoCKks7zY5zcLnSM5PKCOdsNAm9EX_fpYUI-_xz3jeq7nhohRBpfUBf-NU> .

Predicting Fraud

 

Integral Ad Science claims it can help advertisers in programmatic media fight back against fraud with its latest solution, which uses predictive data to spot deceptive activities on websites. Read more here. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001hyeiuOBT_R1yONiHYIKt6FqjAyDv6hNBqiDhPzw4WALB8bYpCs6thHGfMB4CDgIENhDxQ9ZHbzx_bl3EXidftv_x5i89_n5cW6Wtn3iNywEzTXp_PVRxgeXRbUmOYkMOH5kftjD2GEFymOQtW1W-DSSSiUXo0Ryb> 

 

... And Remembering Fraud

 

Meanwhile, John Battelle contemplates the fraudsters of yester-year, drawing a link between today's fake impressions and the shenanigans that played out in search circa 2004. "Think about the history lesson -- an emerging new industry, one that was upending the entire marketing ecosystem, was operating under a constant cloud of 'fraud' which may have been poisoning nearly a third of the revenues in the space. Yet billions in revenue and hundreds of billions in market value was still created." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001hyeiuOBT_R0TT7tt9lxZkdlb1HQYb4fv4NPjruP7vPQwv10ZY8ivKbcATc5gBsyz93qzUkUg0d2Z39NpsCH4HmvpsQEg1fLnUA3H956JKQFaW2ltqgCnq4llK565EPSArFUkz1e6F5uk647Oa4fof24wpKHJmqYLvuOeVxD70xTgnV-g_VESJE_V04GS9yfaL_DCHxOFLjCsc-zFBppj_NBJzS6byTmU> 

 

Live To Serve

 

Writing on his blog, Darren Herman sings the praises of the service layer and argues startups who avoid a service model to increase their multiple are missing a key insight. "You want marketers or their agencies to have the best possible experience when using your platform. I define experience by performance and service. This will have a higher chance of keeping them back (and the dollars flowing)." More. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001hyeiuOBT_R050J78a-ziZIOptT88qcSv8qaaDI4fAJ4JhCIWCX5iOM0QbjZb_MwzaYcnb6gq4QGhrverMGhgVZgAuUEy2LpKLlfSI6V6ddsJKQ-IIICNSdTXsfl-RBr7lQADp69GfAgIr7-xXXob92vzA3fviEN9FeryzJMAvaw1EmQsnuX5SVpwRdwnVPj1>

Omnicom Programmatic

 

Dan Salmon, analyst at BMO Capital Markets, hosted a meeting with Omnicom CFO Randy Weisenburger on Wednesday. In a note to investors after the meeting, Salmon writes, "With [Omnicom] having reported earnings last week, the conversation focused primarily on the long-term impact of the shift to digital on margins. Investors were eager to learn about the impact of programmatic ad buying: Omnicom believes it generates higher operating margins, but incremental technology investment washes out the benefit on an ROE basis. Today, the total media buying and planning business is about 11%-12% of Omnicom's revenue, while the still-small programmatic piece of it is profitable." Read more (PDF) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001PEBJn94ROtCil9pZ-fq-P5hKRpnUL5eDS-dVT4jVdElayT7bgfYVTnBjERtmltleCUxTsJxO3tiKtY8eciJpYpD8W_umf6wj4EUfjrJgilz-4joBmYXQ74SUtju_GmBqiHQXwT-zCuFx76KDtps0lrOhiXWlh88qriMBBEgQYzuMbtXxMcz8DSds0xtDoIchwPU72FOc0DU=> .

 

Facebook Parses App Development

 

Facebook continues to build up its mobile business by acquiring Parse, an app development tool for Apple iOS and Google Android. Parse is particularly focused on paid apps, so this could be a bid by Facebook to move away from a clear mobile ad strategy and ecommerce offerings. Doug Purdy, Facebook's Director of Product Management, says in an official blog post that the two companies have already been working together and not much will change in terms of Parse's branding. What's the appeal of owning Parse? Purdy writes that Parse "removes the need to manage servers and a complex infrastructure, so you can simply focus on building great user experiences." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001PEBJn94ROtDkQXTV4ApC8qxHRbXH3L0cJdlT0iB90bSv06zRkz7AaUu4kzg62Fq84QwpxR2TcdDNc9xOmEV0XVPu3rRDlSFFtdfOacqVn6WcKQ7xegs6fLH8ug4gcFu0ugQ3a7gL0dd9r5R8uadXpd5qYCMcPZKwWSaGNEi0Ntw79PYPYNpPZppCLaVZs90cnbRaK8Ff3Ec=> .

 

Mobile Growth

 

Although highly fragmented, the audience for mobile apps has caught up with similar-sized audiences for other media, according to a new study by mobile analytics firm Flurry. "We conclude that the U.S. audience that is reachable through apps, albeit more fragmented, is now roughly equal to that which can be reached on laptops and desktops," writes Mary Ellen Gordon, director of industry insights and analysis at Flurry, in a blog post. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001PEBJn94ROtDOAT7A4aYg8evsr96-Xb3iBlfBATFnixpbuM-6OkD8F8tGfWGGHcBaNKT7xEatX3IxIaSnqIeYQDek4Xjigs2hpDWfTLTgOEzTJgUCR4PadbODLFc7mybm2GOkWNCKXtry1iqiP19RzqbXmC4d3GfC3XjAcgFbTCuPi5a2EJimoqzjPL6jnTD1> 

 

Cookieless Retargeting

 

Sequential Media has teamed up with supply-side platform Beanstock to bring cookieless retargeting to desktop and mobile with their domain relevancy algorithm. The platform, currently in beta, also claims to prevent "data leakage <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001PEBJn94ROtBIFomvb5howsDryAk7uW3JAmFKbofr1dGntCFn-yR15-eahpMe-MAl1G-fnraCpYaoxsZPHgGwvAq-bRLtS2a_yo_gVpE-D0-g0o6gP1XDbNCZNorfkDtB5whzG9ElT8BbiOrbWlleiCYhtpTn4jdEDqz0mehuk5s=> " for publishers. "'Do-not-track' is forcing the issue and frankly doing retargeting a favor, as there needs to be a way to scale without cookies," said DemandBase's Louis Moynihan. Read the release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001PEBJn94ROtA8xwtJhuLCjbIsN1vj2Xon2GuPxyRC1YMqk80t7fsmfket7XsFABhqEh6rH70NKXkT88RqFPA8RQe-1c1OhnS1fdxCfOtvFCntfEdupyJBLD5x3qMyNrzkg-wetG3bPk9GhM588C2rYmnAKtX0jHLrq3bhnbRod1HqkjQ9zXi6buAIjJ9lKcnS> 

 

Russian Display

 

Russian search company Yandex reported that its display advertising revenues grew 48% in the first quarter of 2013, which comes to 648,000,000 Russian rubles; in US dollars, assuming this editor has done his math right, that equals $20.8 million in revenue. Read the release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001PEBJn94ROtCOn_7wMfd9qkiUrrUusJ3rIvdP4EIbvJD4IokFD3-K1pAKDMbDGcX2Ngdo0VqXqx2RAZZLbX3UyUEqGGp-3PS1UqipjRhlGU4yYcY-M7YxuB6bNm4wC_FFqKn6ylbkxQJ9EQILyBNzGouVxIqr_BZE>  The company grossed $257 million in the quarter overall (for comparison, that's about 25% of Yahoo's quarterly revenue). Nevertheless, under-the-radar Yandex is growing quickly.

Censorship Requests Increase

 

Google released their seventh Transparency Report <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001PEBJn94ROtBjbVxvtTKh9QOYDevDR8mJgF-14UN-rIg2XRxSvdhTc5gy_L9C17rQARlyWHWsymz8BmWoO_NaK6XRHLeWG5HKsWs8huFboSCRiNMkos45KWsjgLymULmuFnNDJLBvPx8=>  - which outlines government requests for "censorship" of internet content - and saw that the numbers have skyrocketed: "As we've gathered and released more data over time, it's become increasingly clear that the scope of government attempts to censor content on Google services has grown." Specifically, in the span of five months Google received 2,285 government requests to remove 24,179 pieces. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001PEBJn94ROtCLAB2EexvmtM7BnT9cgPyjU93ype9h7bK6lrNZygJJZAxnnI5xTCOsamfn3L8azsEOyp-EL5wk4JsqXGy-JVNSxGHHTU-XD6DWSKw_ATMagakyhtaGulsdPCMlHO1O9nFjoqwDpFnG-fBPLJn2RrO50Ryy4xBlZRNGgPr0DdoaHZgP1Qf2-NKr>  Related: As you may recall on Google's earnings call <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001PEBJn94ROtDpU61C5xQeav9akURK167W1Ut6bggaeTA_QyykXN9nQXZjluPpmv5JHDLLa5_myTokL9Has8uhpE3BZSbEfPCF7K8l1KGC7xQsfxBrPluLHMetB4oxUNPARkhg1cMDp0DD0pHqPRQUatdUF56NYTTQfa-Bj5Su0jqjI4T47vq-tAn98e9p5VgJpx7JPTg9ox_q-EYzawbv4g==>  last week, the company said the removal of websites with pirated content from its ad network meant a short-term revenue hit for Big G in Q1.

 

The New Data Scientist

 

The demand for data scientists - people who have the skills and training to pull business insights out of big data - is so high that startups are stepping in to fill the gap, observes AdAge's Kate Kaye. "Their goal, in a nutshell, is to automate tasks once assigned to a data scientist or teams of technologists, making big-data capabilities possible for smaller companies," Kaye writes. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001PEBJn94ROtBhwj-oZSdjWiZiJbAiJu5wao0pgMRiU8fPjmlD2m9HsCZRKpYHRENWjiNZi8NdqNQWxNVLHd9oqQDmzLbpH6182AfvF-CT6XNqR_uDdXRxMTuW5zZkU5oDUehf5JRTso20AU_zGI1pcmSjx6wLeHTMr_DzCc1j7tjP-0G8B3I7FR7cG-pPfb8j9fKSiHLoHSlI1_b57r0mRiIYD12CdHJDFJVJQNxKbOI8g1TUIZTXzDdEGujbEJAhpT4-pP5-IpmRtXxYuC8VaEDiSnVFr-Rs2PgaXRvkNstrhUXI3_Am2waEqKr70CbT> 

 

WPP's Sorrell Bets On Google

 

Wasn't it just a few years ago that WPP Group CEO Sir Martin Sorrell was calling Google the ad holding company's "frenemy?" Well, whether or not he regards the search giant as a best bud, Sorrell predicts that in a few years Google will get the lion's share of its ad spending, with News Corp. moving from first to second place in WPP's media expenditures. Techcrunch's Ingrid Lunden recorded Sorrell's pronouncement from the FT's Digital Media conference. Sorrell also noted that digital now comprises 34% of WPP's $72 billion annual ad spend, rising "from zero to over one-third in about ten years, the age of Google." Read the rest <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001PEBJn94ROtCgfTZJ7anFXD-6KSKnnN9LgnbnbU_jFjjTnjMgvdSLV0a20miRvE33bk6npUtErD61WtgUbfEwCQGS-v-8w9KFuGoD6Hl724XZTQwnSDmn6IGjOp4ueGpI_UKZxOUP-EWPOyIlvtMFKvqFVJbbJOnQ5esoz_PZ5zjaOHMD06lV_m5HIBtFzYkdFdN0jlrXlWYgyMFt5fmz79RHd1ignqMN2Icka7s7TTPJIWBdISNWRpAxN4D-T6Rn> .

Amazon Ad Net Rumblings

 

Reuters describes some campaigns that have run on the Amazon's secretive ad network since late 2012. They included Kimberly-Clark (Huggies), Ubisoft, and an unnamed movie marketer. For the latter, "data on purchases of related DVDs, books and music on Amazon.com helped identify potential customers who were likely to see the movie at the theater and ads were targeted at this audience." Performance? "Above average," said the source. More. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001UXhBiAexZrfoxHARI22fYmNVtnm1q_RUW1qUmgmSqSugil_w7e2wb487n_nYbhINTLR7RKebV_b7GNZUwZCwFnoJmZp43vkotqnUFU2mkurobBJ80dV6wU-LjkyKNE7HMqPm2Flxw3lWd83umQhtZs2l0rNGhyghrJZ-v7bkgBe6jM0BSPKLWfz8K2tDW6KJKWRr1i_mHh4=> 

 

'Do Not Track' Negotiator Plea

 

Last year the World Wide Web Consortium (W3C) brought in Peter Swire to mediate between pro-tracking and pro-privacy interests caught in a tooth and nail battle over Do Not Track. In a Wired piece he describes an escalating "arms race" that threatens to topple the process and end in legislation. He says of post-cookie "fingerprinting" tech, "Browsers are gearing up to disable or reduce the effectiveness of such fingerprinting ... leading to yet another round of aggressive tracking tools by advertisers followed by blocking tools on the user side." His plea: Let's negotiate. Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001UXhBiAexZrcQhIqktSUnEqURNLRyLBq7FcLs4l2vZ3SFwl19FO0naNxwN6cWKl_AYWfHpiEaYrVp1tfsbQloujwOgz0uhC7HlDtf8kSDQxw2qkMX0ZTc54CGgmEKKf2000gNPRwMMlePGlK68f8DcsrTSBp2uuYJ> 

 

Predictive Analytics And A New Integration

 

Adobe is injecting predictive capabilities into its Adobe Social tool to help users boost engagement levels. The new feature <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001UXhBiAexZrfRgX8ZOO0cueb79nTlRny1RK5ctBU8Umv_58lZlv0upaYdkz-HTMOnE8zn2D9MWSVhza6Tx81-4pK_KdkBK8eMweRW73w8V3v8qnIpLxLB1Z61cAsoWNV6bH56Wl9twM1IWj5cn_rkSDw_rqYeJ7d3skAWeID7wCujQKdiXFNnKnrLiBH6YmtWKX7V3f6KDRQ=> , which will be rolled out this summer, uses sentiment analysis and predictive text mining algorithms to make timing recommendations and engagement predictions for brands' social media content. Adobe has also said that it is expanding its partnership with marketing agency SapientNitro by integrating the Sapient EngagedNow platform with Adobe's Marketing Cloud. More. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001UXhBiAexZrfKzD6IlUGvHx8vEa9ejZboO7ZR6Ryq9gv2S_nQL_RUDRv84eFLMyOUC1ktUaL4cjhRhZ20NCz0SkEpQO2oqqX83z50lD5Tjonb3E0p1g6Fcrjva2ByEmMtDhf_uPVCXDqq8DUlRLhUoaf6OiF2m8sZ9n0eOxUy3NWQQzqk8BrX9rcoLMDf9qw5PBDHm9GvriWLYqoM60E0nbFUSG6nJIcT> 

 

Mobile Ad Nets RIP?

 

Well, it may be an exaggeration to say that mobile ad networks are dead, but they certainly appear to be losing ground to social networks, according to an IDC report titled 2012 U.S. Mobile Advertising Market Sizing and Vendor Market Shares. (See the summary here <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001UXhBiAexZrd4MiOzCAaCNtf51zhZWVvqUi-OAY1WMnxpnIRcT57AKOgTEKHZ_AJsEHRHumusWHDL-mNfa4xp3LJUPrcTqpLDzmbakcKq0VAstpU344Qg7nuUsW-zumH7qxluqk8NeBAo5S-1f5maOzTT-h9cD4w9> .) Specifically, the space's former hegemons -- Google, Millennial Media and Apple -- are seeing pushback from publishers, apps and social networks, particularly Facebook, Pandora, Twitter and The Weather Channel, who are now taking the lion's share of mobile ad spend. "Networks, especially independent ones, are entering a difficult phase, in which, with an ever smaller share of revenue, they'll have to compete with publishers, which will only grow in strength," IDC's Karsten Weide tells Internet Retailer's Bill Siwicki. Read the rest <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001UXhBiAexZrfP4XlMimOYhSvWK_QCQE3ZmUnjemilumG3NJ4xqvGA70rMPKeSI99Ji1rSlIGBO0LeWboeZDUGVWmUkDbf1obHEfcEQR2-QiZIFiBEBHQc14fcSHkANlzJBdR6ACUdpUhalh48th8AX8ZpXRmM4h0agrHalgajm4VKDiXD2t1S-Puc6V-BR8VCsadgb-0Ur0I=> .

 

Draining The Agency Brain

 

One recruiter speaking to the Financial Times believes digital talent can make 20-30% more salary in advertising than in tech, but that startup options tip the balance. Aegis CEO Nigel Morris, says this leaves agencies with "relatively few people who have a strong enough understanding of all the different emerging opportunities in digital, with a broad enough brand and business understanding in order to provide the strategic context under that." The end result is a perpetual knowledge drought in agency land. Vibrant's Mobile Moves

 

Contextual player Vibrant Media is expanding into mobile, including images and text-based ads. Techcrunch's Anthony Ha suggests in-line ads on a touch screen might not be the fat-fingered man's nightmare they at first seem. "One of Vibrant's ad units only launches after users highlight a keyword through a three-second countdown, and Irvine said 4 percent of consumers actually do highlight the keyword long enough to activate the ad." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001UXhBiAexZreOPkL9z4fjK9Jf0uuCdTQKBeP-oMfA_ENTMzF_LI--AJqv5OfcVYUocFOZZbxOul9AF0yYZB0oIPD-9ZPDPR4QE7R0NiTxNB653fPqjGon25k6vyDEfxbReP_iHpjZIaaKDj_47EOYBllZWF0l7v73LZeKldriMgMuFZ2qI7iQuQ==>

Microsoft Publishing

 

Microsoft Advertising - or is it Microsoft Publishing? - announced a new ad placement called VersaTiles for its popular email portal Outlook.com. Microsoft Advertising's Jennifer Creegan explains that the ad has three "states:" "Default state: Consumers see the Default state as they log in to Outlook.com. For example, an advertiser can choose to render displaying the tiles with their logo in the top tile and text with more information in the subsequent tiles; Hover state: Consumers can view more in-depth information and see additional images/information if they hover over the tiles; and Click state." See the example <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_VkFk3W80g8QGEXs96wS8pM7xPyZofR3t7zlir4WlgltoUUX2R9iO-mrN2kEF-Is4JJTf-QfDuz4XlR8oDo8TcpEiH5_L4Ys7fwYEGqQKCZ27ODPN3vzxRJDadizRLHyzq3kxGxNDS3uv_HUY3P6Jn2JpTsIi4o3tz7UP-b-JclXj4k9Ldq06Yp3gaA252Ts-8Hd3-8R0pWPz9ej9S0RYU5GjzgN53BzirolmRZ2yGijhHytQy8GyO5qkLjxiB2uYeTQJbJtZ-k=> . Creegan explains in an email to AdExchanger that the ads are all first-party served - and no retargeting or CRM matching of email lists are allowed at this time. Microsoft wants brand budgets.

 

Mobile Ad Networks

 

Chartboost (AdExchanger Q <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_VkFk3W80g-ejlOSiN6G4oj3BVqJA6WiVpGZm531f9edOLpdyQ90yk3BbCUuiHvsMt92z0ENlV8Yyg7gINBAK2ChgqM8mg1aUKRhuwREheqFS3CuZMpb-Gy4mYtmoGVVtxLjhkN53QkUQQwPukmEYg==> &A 2012) is one of the fastest-growing mobile ad networks in Silicon Valley, reports TechCrunch's Kim-Mai Cutler. Its secret: the two-year-old startup "wedged itself into the gaming world where it built an early platform for developers to trade advertising inventory," Cutler writes. Given that games "are the biggest category" for iOS and Android apps, this was "the ideal place to build a focused business." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_VkFk3W80g9OWrAd-I7R_JzNETpMK7619-3MC13647_L806tQSN83y-ORxaCmAw0BakDJ5z680iG_h-biWKrDqN2vA8xPI0zbhCmjQEiUyaIcocFf4gWamFbkZdw-cNTVx4vAb-YbImUKyKF0Z5yD29UDSEgp0jg>

Publicis will licence this technology to third parties." NYTimes.com Pulls Paywall On Videos

 

The NYTimes.com's metered paywall is being lifted - only for video, thanks to the ad support from Acura and Microsoft. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_VkFk3W80g944qnIRnrYBvCKnTXO54wjFOrw8fR5lhPm_KrbPP9QBHDz8Fm63D6C15T8PW1FloVV7d4W8_gwq1frSkaJIC4GZy1mtEbgLPbqRMVZQoAPEd38UGWqzCZu4TNfnbANp6FpgPb_zejJPN1gWRv-Zpq8k5YgThuo3EVJA9a_Aj6NvSbyJGHzaL2mxWyT2dtixPfTqf2f071ZRMnPvID38prK> . Denise Warren, EVP for the NYT's digital products and services group, tells paidContent's Jeff Roberts, "Part of the reason we're doing this is because we're already distributing on other channels like YouTube. Since it's already available [...] it seems inconsistent to keep it behind the gate." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_VkFk3W80g-RxEI8hAzWUwfI2QIB6LQTXJNaX3oagjxkEDo1bQ3-waUhilsaEOFNn_M11bBM08VY3dDbaA6gVoWKWALiscA8BWm7c_30fjH37xVENOFPf2m_VDZ6VnjsV2h-SPLvSRSoVVXFLkvJFXwUI_w3AiV29uN6yc8MpPLcmiHQX4acbeJrUdbcvI9wc1Iri4h96Sptn5D4sKc13Q==> .

 

Commoditizing Data

 

Ad serving, targeting and analytics represent "commoditized, low-hanging fruit" in the eyes of Andy Kahl, Evidon's director of data analysis. Speaking to AdAge's Kate Kaye, he voices concerns that the ease of this business may make big players complacent, ultimately stifling new creativity in the data space. "Innovation can only compete against a commodity when its unique value is understood - it's true for organic fruit, German-made sports cars, and now advertising technology," Kahl says. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_VkFk3W80g_fKDE7SA-iWTOxdiqNmRr93NxbpWNEDNyODM3_jNQUfb4MMLao3SIZQ3CaAdqT8tfoWVQKqEdisaOFeN4kWZ8HW41e_9TPkZrXUma6XX9KlyQoLwacUavVIId0WbRmN-gReJupK2gKlxsEuTfWbAvB4SqbyrIhNepR99ly_VDead-51Kg6hVgfKlr1F2xmJ5UU3_U84eB9u3Tu2OZ8GfMovSN-f2ri_RA=> .

However, with the added pressure on ATDs from inside the agency as well as from clients and Ad Tech players (who've invented a better mouse-trap or come up with deeper analytics or audience insights), it seems only a matter of time before..." Scarcity And RTB

 

According to ad trade The Drum, Xaxis UK Managing Director Nicolas Bidon discussed "how a publisher should approach real-time-bidding - focusing on the consumer and delivering fewer impressions" at a recent AdMonsters event. Bidon offered a use case from BSkyB: "The pay TV operator, which is one of the biggest spenders in RTB, recently revealed it now serves 15 percent fewer impressions year on year via RTB, while maintaining a flat budget, and has seen sales rise five percent as a result." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_VkFk3W80g-8vqgOgyI60Es2J_6Xh0AOshC6fjNUYRBn2QlMtE905pctLnKgLcIq1VwlhnpWh7TqAI_8y1U8XjTyx7d4THgBx2fXIDfh2kBlHcmCyL7XOgaFELp2IK-Fj1jLXCWmLMfZlMKDkDYNZ5WEAW1tvyJlI8e4i8UU50k4jt-aIP629LCVmp31jvz7xedi5YsuuPbtdKvCDjRK2ycGvDY8BZjmejuH8_1gjRKl33ZWo1R-q6UVo1rTtWtz> 

 

Surprising Search Spend

 

Kenshoo released its Q1 2013 Global Search Advertising Trends report, showing a 15% increase in global search ad spend for the quarter, compared to Q1 2012. Ad spend naturally dropped from the fourth quarter holiday season but continued on its year-over-year growth trend. The average cost-per-click in the US was $0.38, while global CTRs were up 62% year-over-year. Additionally, mobile devices accounted for 19% of clicks (10% from tablets and 9% from smartphones), but only 14% of ad spend, according to Kenshoo. More findings in the full report <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_VkFk3W80g8c0LhS9K6ymajQABS9-yHjCMvhA5pVReH6cw2GxX5tQTygr7V4ZbrrTUpHjSpngQ_VsJPRGqaTODzpaON3EA70Rqy4W6LnM__Z4bECuo0k0enWMnsOAZChGr2v38f9f68=> .

Images on Facebook's Timeline are about to become stickier. ThingLink, a startup that lets companies embed links, annotations, videos and purchase capabilities in images, has integrated its technology with Facebook, reports AdWeek's Mike Shields. "The bet is that users will be more inclined to share these souped-up images," Shields notes. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_VkFk3W80g_u3lUlQc2MPcLOGZNAhuFU8HYE_91Qcr-Ut8ZhLp_XczVzXt5VCLLSQ_sZQn3ucW6T5i_XBtW6R3V5oKJ5N0HzsoK50CQQfcnkLjDDKr8fdCMfvS6BRO4mzglmUN4dOkABhSQAYPB4YuUm1OA6R0XE1K2vTQQ56a4kdpaqnQP8r_1ridKJedvMzZlcj8zfnwE=>  Will this be an extension of the Instagram ads strategy?

Bots And Ghouls, Cont.

 

On Adweek, Mike Shields wades again in the bot muck, outing properties and networks that appear to benefit from fraudulent traffic. Media6Degrees and RadiumOne alerted him to sites with large amounts of audience overlap - suggestive of bots. Mevio.com, Forward Health and 2Blue Media Group all make the list. Since February, "M6d has noticed 500-plus dicey new sites popping up on various exchanges-and collectively, 40.5 million bid requests." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001H5V-lTahFEtWs4VRKnbyvIAwAvj9-D_nVerq2x2GSX0C2sSBIerMkh1A4W69tzNnqRHiC3BrLlN-vHcFdfYdzuvhkzt0PJUuRYCqXOeqMEgHPQD0XwqRtqiMDzmWCPBRUCGbK5iK_q7fPHzuBKkeKEKa3-qMJtbDsNSNWO2X4a9H1PD5WBhb2mcR21eCCFlNvS1ePw35vdRdBFQGYfZubuGOx-D0BbmJ>  You know it's getting real when the IAB sets up a task force <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001H5V-lTahFEtO38KwxLfZfPDWixWGTa9GA3XyaXJ46I0oNtNk4sEWXMrFx9ld_uZhHitHt7gdSYzUwLqPQ0neH499vUR9VR9SeamTK9seM9g7Cu5vvdFue0tOIu7Td80c0P6o34Gk4qmh_Nu61t2Senh1w1Ykiv5IEp8P9zp-6AIXKsKWJZ4jI0fQ8zKMFLjLYuDHhDJqY6TNtpT_OEsmUMunfw06z2Kg4PsR9lRROS0=> .

 

Tumbling For Ads

 

The six-year-old microblog network is taking the latest in a small series of bows to the pressures of revenue generation with the launch of mobile ads on Tumblr's Apple iOS and Google Android apps. The move comes a year after the PC version of Tumblr rolled out "Radar" sponsored ad units. In an official blog post, Lee Brown, VP of sales for Tumblr, says of the mobile ads, "It works very simply: Every now and then you'll see posts from our partners as you scroll through your mobile Dashboard." Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001H5V-lTahFEt26Z17BMOPEk6Xi0-o5zKtyQKCvG4jqh4txrtZ885YOjnreABxASpoLggWfMphjUEbIm0xQaWaa1SlyBXDNy-X4kawsXrzime0IZbF4xOATtyoxr9Ni2dF__V8SqsckYo_r0P72K92rvnz9NowdRXLUunE8cjGPKuZp5_FVU7euxdjAhiPzplXLG4fy7qabds=> . AdAge's Cotton Delo has a few more details, noting that users will see up to four ads per day. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001H5V-lTahFEvsBygQ1M8I1CIvkqR05JrgaXEGbqFcu6XIYYSbiDVTLXc6oPM_NNak5MAs8_FdCAq9g_4kPlVDwYb1pjwXfs48qx1HPFsX1UBn0mNTZPIOFpf88YcLnKPyjOVF0xu2nbegQO9IPbpeU1jscWQ20D3FyT1EwUy21yopqqmZelKcNORBGQcB1avy9Zys4gS1k74=> .

 

MarketShare's Predictive Funding

 

MarketShare, the predictive analytics player, raised a huge $38 million round to help promote the expansion of its existing technology. No word on whether that means acquiring outside companies or simply shoring up what it has in-house. LUMA Partners' Terence Kawaja and Brian Andersen served as advisors on the funding. Adam Hopkins, Managing Director at Elevation Partners, said in a statement, "We increased our investment because we think the team has nailed it, enabling marketing to be accountable for business results and manifesting itself in the form of rapid growth at the company." Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001H5V-lTahFEtX6Yn_gvypwxJ5ISpQ84sAEP3NOSAqnDP-eM3Mn2hEPcnzQRYgb661-5C-WEZ3iUTwtZR7HDNkf4eriJYvhNHt68egTnh8NjXFJwhy4e299UefJrZqaaj3el2Wei8v4nHT1QYMD_DM24Ebiv22xD98az5XYhkv87vHfxjNvlStf851S03B7W4tfV6S0hHEZNK4E-N1HisJ6C7xV-iyiPw9jMA8Vhfe36O-OB5EtNXbnIRq85gD0Bl69xLUO03jx9yPpQph-XuwqXfzxR6Qz_f0> .

 

Out-Of-Beta Retargeting

 

Google announced that its previously-announced <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001H5V-lTahFEt8XzQ0u19s-wMeic2eOCyk3TCaUM9hRp5bff7H579hMdG_-49mQ6CHdHiQUnGNMSn7LY7TkFQjzf96TYozTEKpL2PQIa7K1YWBf4T21jt5u4GMbsikJyjnjq9_VyH-t2BEnbkGasau6reuGDWtS2tAnCtbwD4bz1FvETwVPlQ40x6TJ8BnVNY4XLMyjeL-Ehg=>  search retargeting product is "out of beta" as of yesterday. The DoubleClick Advertiser blog explains that the feature "allows advertisers to use insights from paid search clicks to remarket to audiences across ad exchanges via DoubleClick Bid Manager, or the Google Display Network (GDN) -- all with a seamless, tagless workflow." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001H5V-lTahFEu48LUHKWE1CkDpMSviZ1iRnJ4ZFnRGVUjph8C4Z6bb3VaMUh5kFfMNUWJ39E8s7rgd2Xn9kMksJjP0cGzaqpItuvrjth0h745mdxp_3msBeCgu7iyF9eU0qI6coizlavnnCPO6eeuaUObGdEnjUlVRqsCtJk1Xk_UIDcPFhLNmXdrPoliW0REnBAoLdLa4OhyXyoHRvnQthw==>  So, you can take that paid search click cookie via your Invite Media (now Bid Manager) seat and target audience on Right Media.

 

Eyeballing Ads

 

Eye-tracking vendor Sticky is taking the question of whether or not consumers have seen an ad to a new level, reports MediaPost's Joe Mandese. Eye-tracking technology is not new, but what makes Sticky's approach compelling, Mandese notes, "is that it doesn't apply it in a laboratory or a resting facility, but in the real world, in real-time, while people are exposed to ads online." Find out more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001H5V-lTahFEu2RDrxR2TvlD3ebZJDp0uTcqu8zfflGW1rShDbm27_zpaN-KzYyYpOV2qr8mmDu0LYpOu2kSoYqzjMbEGQpKdVAaSdGWDDhB_3oSe0h1DFWAIo5yw9cjKlO5S_ImLsdmnc13OlRPsRvbixRD-3kH5t9t9cyFD8WbcPARyywwOKD9OrRGHgNA_S64IiccfkCIyCa0CN3_loO5MABz_HbYg99a2HQB_gM4X4Z6vzVgBbnGpcpQsgrQnoaKgOcJwoEISReG6QaQA--lPeXWntdwSAivAb2vdDtddTLirS0O-2rxCfhv_KMnu8ytX57vR2T_g_LnknEJ8_Pbhxg25B7lxyTIizc7FJ3qiInXcFVyk03r0WS31p89SPxqCik40nheyIDvSgXWFArP09JCdaxj5ADHeQHX1b1gHZaRTyu6UYn6KY6SaTigk_OP1N9fF0-D0=>

Twitter's Big Ad Deal

 

Emily Steel breaks Twitter's new ad deal with Publicis in The FT. She writes, "The arrangement grants [Publicis' Starcom Media Group]'s clients, which include Procter & Gamble, Walmart, Microsoft and Coca-Cola, access to preferred advertising slots on Twitter, research and data, and new products, such as an 'In-tweet mobile survey' programme that will allow companies to poll consumers for real-time opinions." Read more (subscription). <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001H5V-lTahFEtbEOt_c85zozpodeNeivXIP0Tla66DKbTqharGSGSMIfj1iefDAf3NbbtllALezoLq6mThWR8H82LftK9FGmm4k9_bseiXhi8sgnVy_b-6aBPIFfqALx8qEHbEiYGrY9eNl_i5SKSvqxW8GscX3lOz7JKIp5mefNXXsCvdohWGIxmrnzNNom1c> 

 

Pivot of Yore

 

Fred Wilson on AV C writes an "angel's view" blog post about a bygone ad tech pivot, when behavioral ad pioneer Tacoda switched from a publisher to a network model: "TACODA closed a few big deals early on and got validation of the product and the market from that. But it got harder and harder" to close these $10,000-$20,000 per month deals. Three years later, Tacoda had crossed $50 million in revenues and Aol was writing a check for $275 million. Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001H5V-lTahFEuwZjswxzRMUOkgUq0S5rqGcVcUxyx7zptJoH2Zcl_f7ebbqRW3GorCNXo7suUhshVzi9VBUVSPvCYa24zAverQO7HVdiB7n71F4fvsEQWu6GuP7DxoN9e8xYPvkYTvKkrQJqv624yvI0NdBfCvG__EftnB_vTz5FVCmbX40g87oAWX4M4P4c2aJKYijIlCuVA=> 

 

Algos As Editors

 

Roger Wood, founder of the (Art+Data) Institute, and Evelyn Robbrecht, a content design fellow at the Institute, co-authored a piece on paidContent, pointing to a recently developed algorithm at MIT "that can predict topics that will be trending on Twitter hours in advance. Similarly, startups such as Content Fleet and Parse.ly use algorithms to identify emerging popular topics on search engines. This way, a publisher will be able to create content with almost a certain return on investment." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001H5V-lTahFEvUcx5K_c5g0XZcgoLdXcRkiltDHXTkBSoGiurk_cHu6D82SvhLILIygJra3ayD-BMov9KW905ieD90phWwVWj0m_D-0z53DGT59pW-ckErU7hh1x7OEiN53-3nprZ3_pn8ccVQNp386_hm5RgadMRl-I9ty4dH57EBWV2lQsyG3jIebB3tYYi8YrdBw4d477idCXzwnCFJyDiMVqRAYCvi9a540xeI_GaUEJQCvUF4Qw==> .

AdBrite Inside

 

Five engineers from recently shuttered ad network/exchange AdBrite have re-emerged at Intel Media, reports All Things D's Peter Kafka. Intel reportedly scooped up AdBrite's former CTO and four other employees to work on its TV-over-the-Web project. "I'm told they will work on data and analytics projects, which will include everything from ad systems to content recommendations," Kafka writes. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001QmIvUCO1YQ7C-T-uCOreY3sGXOEPKBBbHyjrieFxzp2hSGQEKOhZEfznxV1zR8ZTthth4SeUNV_H9nryVh6l7MNhUPxirzeNbbJhCoZLVXbe0sIyGe7-xwVbcGNrGoIUTLDrSNAyoGOj87ikmYj1u3O0-BoKvJC9YfkuTACUI3WBbRVy_K9X4Wtzng_h2YfNrr2gQStXBoVdGgxN2PwCFw==> 

 

Fraud Is The Advertiser's Problem

 

On Venture Beat over the weekend, Adometry CEO Paul Pellman delivered an op-ed on what needs to be done with ad fraud ASAP. Pellman writes, "Among our clients, which include large and small advertisers, agencies and ad networks, approximately 16 percent of monthly clicks are invalid (...) aided by sophisticated blocking lists that have been assembled to weed out known offenders over several years." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001QmIvUCO1YQ5peOloLr0EiByJyIovCrJIzjjkFk9H-OT09l0LVs3vfyvGxmbiqCd_Q6k973so_JP8pB508oZWzxFeL7hzMlWOpk9EY7O22W5CMj-DS8V78bvGciv8W_cEDNy6v9BGpTXFMCbsh2gqoJiVZUi6CsBX6mUvtkAc_rKKqbD7dOMj4qNfxD8I7jDIolBDUkqKIHo=>  Ultimately, he thinks fraud is the marketer's problem, "Instead of solely relying on ad networks catching a higher percentage of fraudulent activity, advertisers change the game by developing new measures that only reward good behavior." AdExchanger has seen opinions supporting buy <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001QmIvUCO1YQ5-dKm46-ynnLRaLIYSzReRmQv9NyaUAVroUeCQGOuiGJ90O9ubrO0LUJPc4SoHDHoq-0vp7zqOXDyD2t8MoVpbdpoOB7ZcuMYRkbHMBnqxBc1wZhO_vbu33WDgEAHUYmZHB7taO2rEqQYFRg8aQY9aH8ZqpRcl3uRh1iUxjRtsTvrbcr3Emj1ZGNq5bW1rYLGkN7E079enQg==>  and the sell <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001QmIvUCO1YQ4JV0jgfB3diTgPB2Sdqs7Nj-FkoAmCnf14PpaFtZgAiy00HeFZZjjoh752SFzF0hsfkoL4KhiXjrvETUuMzphTauStSDlyxVlhR-d6acrSPezzo3D3WOR0Npti-m_XShVTk6Ni_ru9be6L2hatmHgWNvXh8KPso4p0zc2uYhiNfEBrKLAH_yDKZ-QigUKJYd_JvbT3iyORkA==>  arguments.

 

IPG Reports earnings

 

Interpublic Group enjoyed slight organic revenue growth in Q1, citing strength in emerging markets among the factors. Read the Q1 details <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001QmIvUCO1YQ4-o2Ysb9PQopHP7-gq24fCDlmK9X7B_Vo7A2JV-6sypaQ8VEFzpfD_xPkbvBGTcIaircYtNZ-lXd0TmZW9jril4_0s-d95-OxfCXr6HNGn7ApD3mHSt8fPFse9UEux6tbBlpaBAIMDdx4RjbLucQxXVD2hET-HuGtCF4ZHD5IxqA==> . Pivotal Research analyst Brian Wieser reiterated "BUY" and wrote in a research note, "The potential of being acquired continues to provide additional support to our target." BMO Capital analyst Dan Salmon tells investors in a note: "All of the black clouds have cleared [at IPG], another key debt retirement is on the horizon (the 10% 2017 notes in August) and consistent share repurchase is increasingly the norm." Read it (PDF) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001QmIvUCO1YQ5iUjPRrbSkhdNj0kWWSzrZon3hITj_ABPZYU3WdGrrGQ7cq5YXswZ1uZk4QKgWqXOHNGzfViOfHegrNooe9E9Pb7Ao31n-nvWlP_6Q-wEHO0kGj8XzOpeLH9QFpy3tdcdgOy3k8JgW3nCqntjOGBLkor7AlycTpdaDzYotiAMyJO00mUyQFEJDTzLMXZHe97w=> . Also - read the earnings call transcript. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001QmIvUCO1YQ5W22I8dswOHD1GeOer8sk9GYJ7OuRS4MgHeH12tbEihPw6IomW27KBwRwP_XPWkQXxq_cEO4hNDNVMuwD_OXBQQUUXABXS4agq9AjYhkIAky5xH6y9F39MgKc9uZWSv-j9ewFgL9fWrkY5R3CmGKvgq8nDeN1EAae810Pk8gqhZ0qkl0Xmw9WNJUTcik60FxqmuyMhkgBgBBrOf1j_6uRWckJNs9U0Hq4_qPQhWLBlZF1S-oFUBXVzQT5aajmfsVg=> 

 

Yahoo Clears The Decks

 

Yahoo is shuttering a number of products you probably never heard of - Upcoming, Yahoo Deals, Yahoo SMS Alerts and Yahoo Kids - as the portal whittles its products down to what it thinks people will use. In a Yahoo blog post, EVP of Platforms Jay Rossiter writes, "We realize that change is hard, but by making tough decisions like these we can focus our energy on building beautiful products for you like the two we introduced this week - Yahoo! Mail for iPad and Android tablets and Yahoo! Weather for iPhone." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001QmIvUCO1YQ7Cp9KKb918xbx2WKZPeQWuARtPneXS81bcHZH6uGUYl2h1O61mWJWM8g_E1h0H4O-vPja5MXRtkbXK0rujRHupeNw0ReBrGE5OpxF3N76jByCZzbDYiq_OqPFYXWATTvL-HSCDmalALg==> .

 

IBM Moving To SaaS?

 

IBM may be moving faster toward a SaaS future. After disappointing earnings, The Wall Street Journal reports that IBM may sell its "x86 server "business to Lenovo as the margins aren't what they used to be in hardware. Read more (subscription). <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001QmIvUCO1YQ6yRYrhw-YTEtyVWNxDrDinlG0XNA_S2XOXOf5oy7zEZm2h0HEuiMZEp9STNBVYZqOZZYAY0Rkg-d2e4Opk9SFu9jbU6wu2vgyF3RHKl2_F5XhOWw8FKtwjdLqsYzPz5Kw9CogidahtCXgGV2FAUGjzauz9l4JnvmYpiQ0NIP8Z_cGqV7aqf6Ug>  It will be interesting to see if there are larger implications for IBM strategy - as in, do they press harder on serving the CMO/CIO with a big data, marketing "dashboard"? Is the IBM DSP at hand? Time for some risk taking!

Mobile Ad Spend Share

 

A new report from mobile ad server MoPub says that "75 percent of spending on mobile advertising during the first quarter of 2013 was on devices running iOS," according to GigaOm's Erica Ogg. Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001QmIvUCO1YQ5c26yl98ujBN5PjzMkomM0ZsSPg-g84eDd3TOjaoSWr-wqpVS44usEb5fxDY3QQyNC3fADmKuEoLbjcjwo8e1aEB8o3TB8qINJi49Gr3SSEqOXvMiBiQ2S3tJ_DAPzLcKaipp5M4woNgHHb8fzVn7iXnivlOzIdpS7e1ogPfZUMURRmnjY0zUGaW1KCwWk_BrNxA92HtoUgT5LCFEpyP7E>  Overall, MoPub says it's seeing more demand for mobile ads at the end of Q1 2013 than it was at the end of the previous quarter. Get the report (Pay with PII) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001QmIvUCO1YQ7GCKVMFFTuFRvZKS8aCVeeZxE8765LUCCEE4TaqhcOjsiVpGLiszW3ve9sEBs8buR8O7Wt2XZqNdNmm4ijh7ZOzBB5ue8CN7BJnZMzqLgZ8jA_uIsDuYdGgyYuqbqDV4jaJKpHA3mOgQ==> .

Levinsohn Explores Vevo

 

Guggenheim Digital, publisher of Billboard, The Hollywood Reporter and Adweek, is considering purchasing a stake in online music video joint venture Vevo, the WSJ's Keach Hagey reports. Run by ex-Yahoo ad sales head Ross Levinsohn, Guggenheim Digital is looking beyond the stable of trade titles to become a bigger entertainment and media player. To do so, Levinsohn has been handed "hundreds of millions" of dollars to go shopping, according to an unnamed source. Read the rest (subscription) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001QmIvUCO1YQ796-JBrBAw1ZFlL6qrdHE7DjT4bzo63WxsCNkHdiFYL3ig3DufJbqij6gLoVb8G7WGVl8kZqhNwmS55kl8Nw76j0XrsqnNd94cljJulzWLf5wn2VFMueQsVJqU-9X-VJ63Z3HGZVSm0CkdHdsfonw0m4kahLsvSb3_WPhENbtNM-kiF0ZpBk8d> .

 

YouTube & Copyright

 

Like a court scene on repeat, Viacom again lost its copyright infringement case against YouTube. The US District Judge who first threw out the suit in 2010 "repeated his earlier ruling that YouTube's posting of...clips from Viacom series like The Daily Show fell under the safe harbor provisions of the Digital Millennium Copyright Act," writes AdWeek's Sam Thielman. Viacom vows to appeal the ruling for a second time. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001QmIvUCO1YQ5ii8G075YkRlhP2kkRWGBHEAlOLcrbguIvm9E5swNNNQrlXXX77839YuwU15W2Jr34ao3rfvDdxgyJHqRwx-JFSpPytouJvOop2OzsWwhnpyZRNCOaDy9guS0ZN164Bz6QIBDXiNCWeoqC-jtzm7EVGtRNdKD7FRemvcZwsml7qm_WTnrL8Xd0>

Shoppable Images

 

Online tag management company Stipple is going after the ecommerce market with its new tool, Stipple Shopping, which enables shoppers to purchase by clicking on an image without being redirected to another page or website. "We don't want to just provide information; we believe images are a platform for commerce," said Stipple CEO Ray Fleming. With Stipple Shopping, he added, brands will be able to "reach untapped audiences who were just looking at an image and are now buying it." Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001CwfdpqwCYlzH9zmVN_sdTb9yAQFo8BaTdONDPurRn-qqNd9JTuYMiCRiUEEP67YA-xIbdbO5PV-qdmQHlR6TI7xPlvyXY2Qa_mi13x5SdhoYz2lmKrfaXz0o0Zu3aJ27s_DZWpkd49N21fInj3MFbLky_YQzb00sJrzfUcd-v1Jz2VsH6dGiiM00vMGYNMbd> .

 

Omnicom Tech

 

Yesterday, Omnicom reported earnings of $200 million or so for Q1 2013 on revenue of $3.4 billion, showing "organic" growth of 2.9% year over year, says Pivotal's Brian Wieser. Read the earnings press release (PDF) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001CwfdpqwCYlwhWOtLfwnPkzVdqjuWFQQbFXTeEEP34xxS72JhLihaS5MS2KU6zNOWFRLV9bVfoWAMZGGMD0vwQu4dRSq2CLHJq_dCzvs6vLfF6nPj-chfX-OtCS7BLhcblw2yFixVDjm_NaAKP4bVqdvaRHSiD5XgEp01fbSFYiwuprSgE8LRohxsb4bocZRr4BKVMvm5YQ8=>  and the investor prez (PDF) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001CwfdpqwCYlxJ_iCyS_tnWoZF7zMnaPH9KwW2ym811Nx-1poXypXztVXYfF9DEBimJBYlCynuquXZJipyFoFH1NDuI3HDivLNOWTe7moJ59Mj69NqVQYzvkn0lqkqEx3MdmpVD1VklE1YPfYGNQu1g0pfVZK3gRPW6RG22wMnVGEykaUgzvHNXcea-7PV9naprc5aMLrY8Cw=> . From the earnings call transcript, Omnicom CEO addresses his company's "media tech" strategy (owning it vs. licensing it): "Because we're as big as we are, everyone comes knocking on our door and oftentimes ask[s] us to do 1 or 2 things: either partner with to make sure that what we believe the individual company will, in fact, turn out to be successful; or we have the ability to make an investment in it. We've elected to deal with quite a number of different platforms, not make a judgment as to whether or not it was a good financial investment because our primary interest is to service our clients." Read the transcript. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001CwfdpqwCYlzxXKgLeC8h71qpA2-tvnKdG_lsW_cx3GMSLQrACYKgHYcyUB17T26-iLEsThqvUYDRoVoSD1_pjcGQZ9n4bGB_jgzpjYmUbqChhIymGkVv3dS6pO1LwKv9OGs1cgikKjg9hzhcsvMtAA96vjAvix5qUFupppC6q5uGLa3HpHgtzl_Snex3PBpexF_qd47eDjfJfOmzr50D9l_fUPnlgJgGTNQSR0oUNZk=> 

 

Privacy Polls

 

With polls, it all depends on who is asking the questions. A new Digital Advertising Alliance study - the DAA supports industry self-regulation in privacy matters - finds that consumers want to be targeted! Adweek's Katy Bachmann covers the thousand-person poll: "Consumers actually prefer targeted ads with nearly 70 percent responding that they'd like at least some ads tailored directly to their interests, compared to only 16 percent that preferred to see randomly selected ads for products and services." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001CwfdpqwCYlxirM7ml8l4IOmLuubN_WcXa58FJaVO2-j7YqOuK0YpCxtwhGgsg9OVPaVT9a8K7LOKRvK1xCTmogyWuAaG1eV-A9RlQzyDzkF7oCM2FL-SjkZK62hA0qWkKRhnZ55fW2Kt36-sYF0ot49pgIgwvHxNYQIJse_Az7IsKFCw2XchzT9Qnb-LKo66DDrw7-jRRks=> .

 

The Reprice Is Right

 

Kristopher Kubicki describes the shift to real-time price competition in a piece for AdAge. He notes that Amazon was among the first to start repricing products throughout the day, but others have quickly followed suit: "During the last holiday season, we at Dynamite Data detected up to a three-fold increase in the relative quantity of price changes over 2011 across major retailers." To protect ROI going forward, ad bidding systems will have to match those quick changes. More. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001CwfdpqwCYlzUHKUWk3F1pIf5GDwJHXe_RU73PVfcG7Fy2pPZmFiT_NKOSc-SZ6WJwvaD04YkZlXRVb2xGMnPYths2MmKEyosHCXm1zpK2T2AcEtEIZsF1mq6FIvniees2pNtQkKedKHOCnJO2JpIkIvRBE2OFvlUEbQlox6latDlRdQxCKPkAoGrlrHF0fRk0bIPUI_5_EY=> 

 

Microsoft Online Services Revs Rise

 

Despite some continued challenges with its PC and tablet product fronts, Microsoft had a pretty solid quarter overall, beating analysts' profit projections but missing on revenues, according to Tech Trader Daily's Tiernan Ray. Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001CwfdpqwCYlwr90bpitel0P1HN93ejUcSBIIIAi86gtdDpOrmtZo7w3YCxGXTvDwtdV9gKDBOa2CKSruAysJgFHhPYkOGETnNADn-RkpW-_ou9_20p1JI6MA5ELxOECNFxxyiWhDekOq4uEaHLyTdN0dMGkTuJHkreK0VANDRB08U0zn8UuOnlTzbKimfWFxgfW5qf5NeT1kYFGfvFWVeGoDNPW9QGeyyiNgNgXO5xKmqpBF1KXiJ5G0jkiwV5Z93LHgusHSIf9Z2iu-ZfI9NNQ==> . As for the Redmond Company's Online Services division, which includes MSN, Bing and its IE browser, revenues were up 17%. Specifically, online advertising revenue grew 22%, which outgoing CFO Peter Klein said was "driven by an increase in revenue per search." Read the earnings release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001CwfdpqwCYlyjFjn7oQc2cmMlZCQyBZHpq_t_nwl_c8x_G8P6tc1I56gVs_duH04JfmCOCe3yKw7Q_WWjJFcQ_khrFXU7faE8zmjEFBRjCJH5Kot1apxsEwURHf1_KgzCMPH8qAF9tz32pKj6kBZSmfqrLa82zHIbpNHvLw6xsHi8Ce0QmnGq16si5qq3FalEINgWE-U4AqeyNQQc_4FX_wOcBCyoTIT-NIca0ko4fVWbeUcoc1MpxA==> .

LinkedIn Adds Smartphone Ads

 

LinkedIn's overhaul of its mobile apps will, for the first time, allow the company to show ads to smartphone users, Reuters' Alexei Oreskovic reports. More than a quarter of LinkedIn's usage now comes from its mobile app, up from 15% one year ago, highlighting the value and the necessity of connecting marketers with consumers via phones. LinkedIn will begin showing ads within the mobile app's news stream as part of a "small test," LinkedIn rep Julie Inouye told Reuters. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001CwfdpqwCYlx8TpprFLrDQCOLX3zZtHh1tJZocZbdP44D4nMxcGQZKIFf-zUVUfg5OOtjHgLiXm0c3vwXOOiOjoWtYdiA3H8P1MGW-AeAJAwJBWwjczmjLxZXeiJEXhwW1PS_SVHUPXHHBRrENFmPAkRDzYU54QBQO0E4yzUhLGLsqatPqLA19ZfEagIRYbahAMS1wTXyD-114zquP7-cNBP49J-25aM8AAm_0pSYLH3cuZuDFw0GdUtAc0HojbtjYpsyQ_Uc7Uo=> .

 

...And More Earnings

 

IBM also reported its Q1 - and missed expectations. "Despite a solid start and good client demand we did not close a number of software and mainframe transactions that have moved into the second quarter," CEO Ginni Rometty said. The business analytics, containing what used to be Omniture and Unica, grew revenue by 7%. RTB Trends

 

Accordant Media has released results from a study of Q1 2012 real-time bidding (RTB) data seen through its ad buying platform. According to a release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Lz_Y9XKSoVG3Dh-ewJYiNccdnrjL7Ei80JhTGsGLUKP_MLrdvLRbaK6ra0Yl5HLLBnsRz7VFeKwM3GtDjwIXuZ0XhDAXIncSANMnEq0pb3nyqbQpmCIW3Rc79kcaC6FhMukRNoANLm0QSPD-TwDtqrO6mWVYqq-Imb6oxd0EvBpNXmfAmJLqKu3bKJiDEjKanrWBulzGo8wnh_otP-nSP5--USEb0QkbfSh6iA-T8D0M4ILc-2IzE39NqOR5BZSzXHbEESAuFBP-9x5R3q7hRCrogFycj0Bh3I8txPhLhxN8hQI075iPOlXZ0vvMt66G> , "Ad placement transparency improved significantly from 32% to 41%" - which seems to mean that Accordant could see the URL/publisher for the placement it was bidding on. Read a bit more on MediaPost <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Lz_Y9XKSoVFsbAlWiorp_q07Wqggu90RuicHD85czaQLte603tOmT9Px4hISVg_WsVmCjX404k6V5ETy_AsNT_gVTx1j0QftCmIcR0DRSuLh8AoJSpVv7vGKuzJQNhh1QwC75dmtyNjfzoJfx7uI-7S7sfaLypNa5M9EaLOIYpuRXcU3nOXYDuDMi_iVljc3GB4H1YMxUB-JoGJp8cN-ZEaTT1P7wvZX7ujfM5RvEO8=> .

 

Twitter Programmatic - Day 2

 

No doubt in reaction to AdExchanger's post about Twitter's programmatic strategy <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Lz_Y9XKSoVG8kx-cpdcXA2zNsUpXCmFmIi_4kJj0m1agL3M8AVMPi8W60DRTLcysnlDIZp3geXbInB_hc8I9zun-DTmrSusYc7jJ7ICxvH9x_zultii01-55g3vaXxQWl5N7kh7fkEPQT2aeirmBbo48oosMhfDTBEMHg8ZskaCC6xkzsqZkdQ==> , Twitter announced yesterday that it's now allowing keyword targeting in its timeline, according to a new post on the company's advertising blog. Twitter product manager Nippon Malhotra writes, "Users won't see any difference in their use of Twitter - we're not showing ads more frequently in timelines, and users can still dismiss Promoted Tweets they don't find relevant." I wonder if this means people will be tweeting "I want a Starbucks coupon" in hopes of a freebie. Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Lz_Y9XKSoVHWJume_zRU54v1ykTt353fFbVw141E87OrLMlkrEBYu7hE5UlwHpRYhV1aPzZUkwngTOHvamv733KuVadzR9yKq_bGfG7NOS6pIkrrKrSgVV8RFPLQ6bN_tI2VxbnWNJYKKKEuT3oqk4NmBYstvc0AoqGpv29X-9aDAC6V0niYBQ7rJTPDZVphdEnSz5xQCb4=>  Retargeting those user cookies through a display ad exchange could be next.

 

The Cookie Crumbles

 

All the talk about Mozilla Firefox joining Microsoft's IE browser in blocking tracking cookies by default has got some in the industry intensely worried about the continued growth. But Lotame COO Adam Lehman says not to worry. Writing in Digiday, he says, "Turning off the Firefox third-party spigot will only represent a 15-20 percent reduction in the available third-party data from Web-based sources. Taking a broader view, as the Firefox door closes, a hundred new doors will be opening (or at least a few new doors with a hundred times the data)." Read the rest <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Lz_Y9XKSoVEnNvHgxXG7dqsGyN8ILIOOT2gEglu7OTk28VRJMKEJHkzbOns3U9lkUjsm0Qx5rqJs8_TRS7AKw_1dIv2UsxCnNeDpRuyQtadCYqO02eas1kP_0UTc75i6HbE4h8C_HfPaDlou1sgoQ3uv9KdaaOXEVGcOUEaGNFM=> .

 

AdX Private Auctions

 

Google is letting DoubleClick publishers set up private auctions "directly above the open auction." The new offering, which follows the launch of preferred deals last year, lets a display ad seller give "first look" access to select bidders - for instance, a handful of agency trading desks. On the buy side it's available to all, including Google's own DoubleClick Bid Manager (née Invite Media). Blog post. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Lz_Y9XKSoVET7K4BrgNyQaluumOyPCrRhj4VyIGG3_GgaK-lVI-EZWY4_RABY5OCXFINCT-8cGM9FOmmMQ17Hm8qYqAj71A46g80u0EGWuBCY0JuTo_2jGMM2Ox1_77H4du2baQ5ZCWVBuv7VcdtN_xIDoFl3p2pVTOdijPeDh3fOeAVbX9UBOQziLFuX3XRd8FbcQLgDak=> 

 

Ad Network Buys A Rival

 

If you can't beat 'em, buy 'em. Video ad network Alloy, fresh from banking a $30 million funding round, has acquired its similarly youth-focused rival DBG. "With the added muscle of DBG's impressive video and CLiP platform, we are further realizing a vision for delivering compelling content directly to both consumers and advertisers and effectively monetizing the value of our top content brands in a new media world," said Matt Diamond, CEO of Alloy Digital. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Lz_Y9XKSoVGPBdImgYMiK962WiGhNKYmh6cEXP8wCR5-tUrnscjYEjTXiwkF-7tHAdTWPcMLK56XdxafL2JLQf4wCsaJ_yjz3qpU7j2_epZhKnl65xseCeed408Kai8bv5_9-wOPXVC1_Cz07Qv8oAJxBP1JZgbrgORjRHgGv0-p-ig4N0Tha0dk3oK8IjcjmtWTSht6J3wLgOiAIQ4HgAlX5_PHxvav>  (via Deadline Hollywood).

About Those IAB Numbers...

 

MarketingLand's Danny Sullivan is taking issue with the online ad revenue growth figures released <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Lz_Y9XKSoVG2YRMxzmsZR7cP8KCOTviCuRkZwPDz03dStt_nu_Qp3Y_1Q_RYzjzyI1iNMCphlHWObG3GSuNqR9xJuNcgaPvUoVGzQERI4g_tM4PJnqSs216fCgsmyx45ez1HTj3C5tHIQE69FX7-BCKWV9tr5Fc7iIyy0FZouFXG8nGKW96D9FS7iu4H3T8rpNs9QpCHQokNCFNjZIyFhg==>  by the Interactive Advertising Bureau this week, particularly the way the ad categories - search, mobile, display, etc. - are grouped: "For example, consider a display ad that you see on your phone. Is that display spend or mobile spend? According to the IAB, it's a mobile spend - despite it being a display ad. The same is true if you see a search ad on mobile. Despite you having done an actual search, resulting in a search ad, the IAB considers that spend to be a mobile spend." Read the rest <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Lz_Y9XKSoVFCPISY56FNjJRgZ26zfjOGBJ4D85KA_gdh1g6O3zY6lIFsVuGISwWVaTa6KuPPsTqubgwjNcDGVsr7OAfY-FAv-p06rBgEYD-vhaeogEg-K3V-5b2Y8ZgK5DfFJ2iFl3PsgIweADX3mXbd1rP98cwHeIeRJUEl9-R7TQa2KV-yIaNbefVpPA5Sy4IcoKzfM4iAxlqVpoKZkTyszxMxKsQUqDu6JFuTYDmf_FZEgy012y30HkEz_ckuKQDZ-cPWllK5F0UzJNfav0wPW7f0z3KHM_Axzg73zFRp3W8gdA_E7Q2M1St8OdBZUaqW9IVwiCCLHE1JvCQm04yEwxM4n_Ez3YospRXIDjI=> .

 

Targeting Exhilaration

 

Social and mobile ad startup MediaBrix bets that serving ads to game players while they are basking in the glow of a high score will yield higher engagement levels. A new product, Rewards, lets brands send players a coupon or other messages when they achieve some in-game milestone, such as a new level. "Rewards produces powerful emotional connections and creates lasting impressions for a brand," claims CRO Todd Bowman. Read the press release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Lz_Y9XKSoVG5YLnSPI6mUEFoX3_xcqZ_pC6979gRsXo3sf7BPsnvjGSlxziycD6ji-d3SewG8Z-SIxXvq6FOnshraq2RvNxPpPHVFd--yRWQGl25xNGEfc66x7HPGMHK9HcpUL5u9mCwnvjYff2fOmhpQ8eEtjGS3QJjqp_89pDBDNvUrxd_bo5OSWE32-kYc4GrEbX9WKOdCFmsy8WpMYmgfc1TiOM66NZc-6_FN7aGPZv4q66HqHZ4bOvuUb3XOvqAsInj6PAHPf2VtYCFfg==> .

 

Publishers' Creative QA

 

In his publication, AdMonsters' Rob Beeler delivers the results of a study on creative QA and the publisher. Beeler writes, "While almost every publisher reviews creative look and functionality, fewer had a sufficient built-in process for the other things that come through a third party tag: namely malvertising and tracking pixels." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Lz_Y9XKSoVEoNSzmJokJpxkHYBneFTexjBuvFQBE7ASKrrv58shp8RI98AcMetg8EWQxrTSCD3rdChgLC-MPVCXU4kAeYQyaiSCYrVY1GV4gl9mUfxlDbGkmkMgiH29wAQds3cq_Ql25KwxDReg0hFKVTIEtdx0BTEllTJrjCZQ=> 

 

Sleepy Local Media

 

IAC Chairman Barry Diller told Newspaper Association of America's mediaXchange attendees that "sleepy" companies behaving like "recovering alcoholics" as ad sales continue to drop off will face extinction in the age of disruption. Net News Check's Michael Depp reports that Diller doesn't understand why local media has not capitalized on the "ability to be so granular and local that you are every possible grain to anyone who lives in a defined community." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Lz_Y9XKSoVEngkxXMslIOpesjxI9u7fVXARJ8YV5412HQKxHVNiJj0bsjaMwtayol1lLbZ9n23MCez_ia4t3JvQjAoOxK7cNAzKsKsOL485KZzH8MX56DNJA9kx2vtAumK6-j3_wnJcAgMxVB3oFCPwmETi_WVv9vpn0NU24yKEnADfifxhhLEfk9GBrpuDgzfOucp4keG0=> .

 

Don't Sell

 

On his company's blog, Upstream's Doug Weaver whispers in the ears of naive sellers everywhere with a list of what not to do at client meetings. Weaver lists one don't: "'You sleepwalk through the first three minutes.' So much happens in the first 180 seconds that really defines the meeting. Yet so many reps squander that time with meaningless small talk and paper shuffling." Read more don'ts <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Lz_Y9XKSoVGAfXnWkn_5CUwAD0X6w_eCF2u_SYBSckzfKWi8nSANKbP4BB6mhbUtRVIytg5ax2_ryyOcZSfCuUKeRZw0wXXseJS1v1U6gAHxNTszn2o9iVjuIJQZShnu> .

Weather, Beer, Ads

 

The term "weather targeting" is bandied about with some frequency, but its meaning can seem a little...foggy. Is it more than predictive umbrella peddling? Digiday shares findings from The Weather Company that suggests media buyers should indeed watch the skies. For instance, in Chicago, "Four consecutive days of below-average summer temperatures will spike beer sales by 20%." Atlanta has its own weather-to-beer quirks. Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001pEwk2B0qy0p5ivwLRtSPnihuULLCv7mANJpAOKL3qbaqetx6s92ER2CcgOIGJ9MDBh0jPmrfQ6SPZ6Aem4JlCXw9-bOAE3jx5wnL0q254p0LZ-Tv7Ske25qg-yzHbLQICfrrZxqudRcG3w-ruRPhjEouRqKCQsZPLEgY7sQwy_w=> 

 

Mapping Credit Card Data

 

Credit card companies are increasingly selling transactional information to data firms, generating new revenue streams and potentially raising privacy alarms. AdAge's Kate Kaye covers a few examples: "Using the Mastercard data, a burger or pizza chain might use the system to push promotions to neighborhoods in which people spend more than the average at fast-food joints." Zip+4 targeting and vague audience segments (e.g. "frequent transactors") seem to be the rule here. More. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001pEwk2B0qy0oRc8L_JH6XlyuliqYziDODpnmWk9N9M4zZPfa_OInzrIBQGNZreHt5nZYmBB_vB1iUhMrCdsPBQnhWGIStgUY9Np4cCqR--yfk84pUX7-SaLyGU-dxPc57_Km5x4mNwbC7W2m4-CbGYxn-w-KAgLdPOFr3PTuSJPqOpKtG0WViXXIhf7lVj0FdHZUm-qWYqtABYJhGQxvF0A==> 

 

Commodity Markets

 

Jeff Green of demand-side platform The Trade Desk revisits the difference between financial and ad markets in a piece on MediaPost. He relates this anecdote: "I was given a stark reminder of online advertising's often singular place in the commodities market after speaking with a Ph.D. student who...had been studying the habits of corn pricing on commodities markets. He informed me that there were essentially over 125 variables that make up the value of corn. With human behavior in the equation there are virtually an infinite number of variables." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001pEwk2B0qy0oGnKRWDZqhxtxMl5tZNfOiHyczs-SU1ngQvz1a0VQHZF8NlY9fvpkcDwcx2vsFGLy90tM6Qgby7u1effgqNdWi14fApI58vaRG6NAAPsO8506yANsZK4NmbAvJLbWLv28ihS4enfzFz4j38nW5GG3kZzoDMMK6wK-LoiMC4_571NN-0JgSpwy5CONaIuP_PJm9bmL57tse61KlbF_0wOSL> .

 

Slow Growth At Agency

 

On Monday, agency holding company Publicis reported less-than-expected sales growth in the first quarter of 2013. Read more on Bloomberg <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001pEwk2B0qy0pghhO_IuhvJNC60wdbTvut5vQNBtfhMzYMgUrG85W8E9nqbQiVw2_4vCtMCnaRlVhB_wtDTS-ywPm9t9RBydTfJycfVfjce8vWC3lKgMm8K5LXy4MusnF87WjNtX9j_q-ucTxra8t3Fwoak6HCPRocIH72XB-qFUPGyb5XEEwwmKn7R7X2pYZVqBt7LSlRVtKuNSamoZDubbICDgQyUkDzqTm5EQ2KfiI=> . Nevertheless, BMO analyst Dan Salmon notes, "A strong quarter of net new business ($2.1B vs. $800 mn in 1Q12) gives management confidence in the back half of the year. Overall, we take a wait-and-see approach ahead of the analyst day on April 23 in London, where we can get more detail on management's efforts to reach its 2013 organic growth target of 3.2%-3.6%."

 

Cookie Crumbling

 

In Adweek, Tim Peterson investigates the demise of the third-party cookie and listens to a variety of industry voices. Acxiom's Geoff Amborn tells Peterson, "In a cookieless world, publishers with business models that naturally collect strong names and addresses and other personally identifiable information are going to be able to...connect into CRM databases. For publishers that have a weak PII story, they've been more heavily reliant on the cookie world." Trouble ahead for some - perhaps the "long tail?" Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001pEwk2B0qy0r34Rx2cYAPgVx_ndXHxpo5V0pySjU3GwKzvDlTmC9t6B3drs_-g146TPQiDNg2UYiwsU5k3NoVwDHy0MhAsz7p-ijVlhgvlrtF9Nf7efiZ3fj27QkWv8VLDYhSmORXopC79WqKn-Y8-rym4mE926jj-yYCsN7y7Fd-dtcw8hOzz4MSLRbQer-f5ef65osWZwpujNOyrmtW3CcYgPSBpF4g>

$egmenting Audience

 

Real-time bidding company Turn has released a new report showing that costs for display advertising, video ads and other rich media are increasing, while those for mobile and social ads have fallen, according to TechCrunch's Anthony Ha. Noting a Turn audience segment called the "digital elite," Ha writes, "Turn says it's the report's 'biggest discovery' - a particularly desirable audience that includes 2 percent of consumers. They see 24 times more ads than the average consumer, and advertisers pay eCPMs that are 85 percent higher than average to reach this audience." Read more about the  <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qRIaplP3t2uz4Qz6Yc4xNsFAdCobx9ozVY-epBR6C04q_IXM82uK68EowA1W3NYohROPqTMQEtPE5SjMTcC3GpYzvtamqsRIRLzAy3NHB_rBELHgsHZaGnqx_1VaFnYMk4k9GLBFB6W5ExQimgg35h3F2zm5KT2CbAo55oQwSWg=> "elite" and get the report here (Pay with PII and first born). <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qRIaplP3t2sPisMGLb0dCZhSmXQshTuZ7v9wxsgak3zDlkErS2d7kbJhcyN8Q7fOqhau7KtBlOz3-JXuq6JeoU5XkQE93xWNvSG_tVokVVYfSLOJy_SIu_ojI0IbzV6X> 

 

Shady Business

 

Relying on the advertising industry's version of a "bake-off" - pitting vendors against each other to find the best one - carries several pitfalls, reports AdAge's Jason Del Ray. Marketers or agencies should be on the lookout for "loopholes that allow firms to game them," Del Ray writes. One example is the vendor that slashes its profits in the trial to get a prospective client's business. "The problem here is obvious," Del Ray notes. "Once they win the business, they will need to make a profit and will have to change tactics to do so." Read more.  <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qRIaplP3t2sL5QcYn8S3GB5IlbHTdpyD3TdOMwOlqO_G1ntmo90Ar2z7pfElgTErwTTYIjM3SzMOlcAhYYNx4CcYGQa2fpL1LMt537RZ3cinmmwdjROn5BAChwflRptEPTro4Kv5aVG2hrmAaXgXc-QcUi4sY1LmqLtYN9JOPEjAeCehbhjEveIp6HH1sRADUr5gBzFLs0tYfkttn-wfaPL767HnT8cjkGFSogj_m5A=> 

 

People, Come Together

 

Brands, publishers and ad platforms need to stop talking at cross purposes, John Battelle writes for AdAge. The core problems he raises are familiar: disagreement over what to measure, an unwillingness to "get to know the other side," the role publisher context should play in the media plan, incompatible incentives. Battelle calls for "a longer-term vision than the next click, the last attribution, the successful exit or the highest CPM." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qRIaplP3t2uIvX4I87WSd-A2oRp5t6t4qqY9HP73fAUFz2ikUkPokHoA_bAC-oGKKzIr1ubOAGEtrtsxT1F25A0dqjWTuE6WF5n6nX6TWLV1H7wP1fl-eF2zmZzd5VESHRapm_S2yjHQo5Wn2STtowgy_koogwhr-hJ3mnwV5b2WK7HFKPXMEIXxKhvmbfRHTxwUL1oBYBePXIo_QgOtqUh9mXL0I4nIyNxYrYxCasbwDRgXlc5-2aZ0_8yPooBG> 

 

Hearst's PubMatic, Programmatic Tour

 

The Hearst/PubMatic media tour, covered two weeks ago in Adweek <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qRIaplP3t2uhB_Ahe27SW-esBE9q9sA9pWVbOta_xhmQpZROieU_ziCWHSa9q0Qg0cUMWXDNTPcbzaXeSUPtQmNH6nI2OadAJPOgEBcho54ghqodclrm2LdDA7OsORB3Uw8MpkOH1CEcIAZE06utBac1ngionG5hfOgbN9bBKlR9Rd3ukS7Qmlk2F0nlFre-3MDoX8QnTjk2gfFHNYtvGasMB3Fbg6gJ> , gets its turn in Digiday. The tour offers an under-the-hood look at the partnership's private exchange, which was rolled out last June, to see how much more valuable inventory can be plugged into the Audience Exchange - as the Hearst/PubMatic system is called - without cannibalizing the publisher's direct sales. "Programmatic creates a platform that allows us to do more with our marketing partners, not less," CRO Kristine Welker told Digiday's Josh Sternberg. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qRIaplP3t2vtBDfDVs8qnAJTweskuglP6BqJEXMuq031YSbRbmUduPSRgI4Us85hh-G6auz66vs05Zx62kv-j7g9jeHAS3W0v-1d1ZtMAY2EfVW5RzJcXGK5WXiigr5QP2nd6ZzJ4dIpWcMPq-9xmDWKrxhqWh4124ARnAPiC49i4P8kM5VG0w==> .

 

The Ultimate Disconnect

 

About three years ago, Google engineer Brian Kennish had a change of heart over helping the search giant collect user data. Kennish formed Disconnect.me to block Facebook from using "Likes" and other tools to suck up member data. Disconnect.me is now expanding its anti-Facebook data collection system to cover platforms run byTwitter, Yahoo! and his former employer Google. In an interview, Kennish tells paidContent's Jeff John Roberts, "The company is at work on tools to limit the spread of data from mobile devices" and create education around privacy issues. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qRIaplP3t2sLYfDOVI5q8s4DObtulPR1xTPsEW9-iu6rycKJnaAE1Pw2vgfH6jSy3K4HYOR19STaMniT6YBzbeEQIYY2sBsq50NnUKmvExBVFMoc636IKzjlYb-6qUuDP6NZ7LQCcM9P8Ed8dNQR0Y6hp3sct76dTBJ3WaLZvjyCQ5H3F7ZdKqZ2rhf0eHtdXX3uGVeaOgXawTcfixRYsBBHHEVEYR0p> .

RTB Charts

 

eMarketer brings its graphic design skills to real-time bidding (RTB) courtesy of new video ad data from Forrester and video ad exchange SpotXchange. A sample observation from the report: "In 2012 the number of video ad impressions bought via RTB exchanges doubled year over year; this year, the number of video impressions will top 100 billion." See charts <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qRIaplP3t2tV2bzZ0mu5y80dDbf0b_KJVpMFwkWV5Pdk3JlsD3OJp97aWM-D_rs2bKttTAzYCHKOaZ7gdOK3grTBIegecwtGJgXZ2evYWiVYJOashh0uoEbHWrAbdcVYJnMAqb3baIx4u7nDt5swv0Kyu6-UbdNSmUzMywHLC9UJmHbP9VqtdonAWeToIWEV> .

 

Mobile RTB Ecosystem

 

Former Admeld mobile exec and current Googler Marc Theerman revisits his mobile ad ecosystem map, originally posted on AdExchanger back in 2010 <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qRIaplP3t2tV2bzZ0mu5yw8CflbAyoZ9IaAammfmbwjG_QnKbJy9mTY-48-F-SJzvF2P0tVj2U2uEjd34SAO1BB6WJDN71lq25Ne2VyK0R2XMkhehz6aYietaXMIdeRblVqLKzZrIslzEgRem-FWbHO284y8LMSDgCRZIgk41tg=> . In his personal blog, Theerman exhibits the latest map update <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qRIaplP3t2tVen0Qo8QoFg5IeXIW6OyNOqZSpbxjLTbeWb2ih0LMHklxGfMDWbnRYT9CY53JoH68HSVogFE6h5lT2KSCsr8bpOV1MNlKkFvteDM1YTIJ7gn9IJihGP2d5fWvwTTsQX8=>  and says that RTB will win in mobile for two reasons: "24 months from now, the majority of all impressions will come from mobile operating systems. RTB is the only efficient way to match buyers to sellers in this exponentially growing universe." Read the second reason <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qRIaplP3t2tVen0Qo8QoFg5IeXIW6OyNOqZSpbxjLTbeWb2ih0LMHklxGfMDWbnRYT9CY53JoH68HSVogFE6h5lT2KSCsr8bpOV1MNlKkFvteDM1YTIJ7gn9IJihGP2d5fWvwTTsQX8=> .

 

Children's Privacy Timeout

 

The Interactive Advertising Bureau has filed a request with the FTC to delay implementation of the Children's Online Privacy Protection Act (COPPA) by six months, arguing that the guidelines, which cover a range of activities by websites aimed at kids, are incredibly complex and difficult to implement easily. "It's a complete makeover and that will take time," Mike Zaneis, the IAB's SVP and General Counsel, told Adweek's Katy Bachman. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qRIaplP3t2se8iwUmf5aKLD8U5kqM20zz73nxQ8I0WYIH132GPsSwgwIQYpYOh9Zx1kz37NNcAsQW1lMaBtb8XL9H0dx8Ex-KG0V19kz_gOUsK8r0nD7aDClgrAX2xjcDFGHAAf8zFLBIaur0pVLSLLxdQXjwlmFEsr6aduy-EcSYevoJr3kXX4-skBZd95sc0-NCHpLYtCCZwYRHhzXOoHJxcFPeokS> .

Trust In Google

 

The European Union has extracted concessions out of Google as it relates to its anti-trust investigation. The Financial Times reported over the weekend, "The US internet giant will revamp its results page to include prominent links to rival search engines and clearer signposts for its own in-house services." But, is that a big deal? The FT says it could have been a lot worse for GOOG. Read more (subscription) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010V9nSNfbz17FWrbOH1s3tcdVNYoSCtU75j3qd-r0_zKN9vbI1RYUEhFYRf8i08fHIA6xGdFCl3hsH6JTG_py9_wySDJQIbfkxlH-OzVrZmH7JQW_KstbW3xCnCSP28MnOSa9jA4-zNA0zsK2g95rdq7e45VLrTZXPfib2kb7-Xu0twNDknLDOA==> . And, still more analysis from GigaOm's Jeff Roberts. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010V9nSNfbz14e_P1dpnjqF17t_p9nS2EE4GB51a8AzG2OI-cWt_BSLAo9KI0tGGgWYJjfWzGiZybZGPtFZB-wEbbivuCe64tMZxV6loqajyfR_t8zf_bchnmyD3JN5X5eN-MoG7-knAItlrDWQf5taxsdMQSPgBsJzrsIFu-Jto1BkDw-rm-Rr8oXbvJUfD1FhwaU1WNoh6w=> 

 

Display Yesterday & Today

 

On Digiday, Brian Morrissey finds that the first display ads were a branding play -- not direct response. Joe McCambley, former creative director at Modem Media who worked on the ad for AT&T, said of the experience, "We believed if we could create something useful, we could be successful..." Read the rest <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010V9nSNfbz17M9CY5rVK9n39QSg9V-QqgMP9HKPu6MJvmvcl3TnW-t0q8PC5DCdLcNqoEF-txs4QYrny5NlgLrH4wzI1G4MhFOcIWpacXxAMrrhu_PdvqOckHxQYT-rYD7FYEwvFcGJMDylJoXHSroYM_CQz6zj5FLhmOFWhfztQ=> . Fast forward to today's display ads, and Rocket Fuel's Eric Porres says <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010V9nSNfbz17j-KpuoJ_ZQmY_fswoCwuAUvvyvYm9s8E3yZvU_1w4yp4VL3yEaxVe0nyYJ0py2Opqb7S4E08s6e1MMr9-DNk2Brn478Fw0bk_4TZ2ywTo0vaLeUllyuqIFKPP1uXMaH9nS8TK7WSQiNQhNRHS131ZQFvJTuwWjhVbB1w_Q9Ro9im0vD0D4JC7UPeICFO9EjTPfeZlDaKIBBjFEPw-Pf9N6WbaWKdhwvuEApBwnydt6IyisYXLoWl71-GWgu3x204Ki9-hPpF8_RPr71eF6l4ouTJ03Lq5h4IpdwW67Sm2Iw==>  that programmatic media is delivering "at least" 50% incremental benefit to campaigns over the old way of doing things (presumably the old "bulk buying," publisher ad networks of yore).

 

Mobile Ad Choices

 

Evidon and TRUSTe are attempting to bring the AdChoices icon to mobile display. (Is it going to be really REALLY small?) Ad Age's Kate Kaye reviews the efforts and sees torpidity <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010V9nSNfbz177bkhTR9c5rPZxpycqwBwOVyNn_lTkvXDYWXgkb0zgdytr60CzrpzubQci8D84yVNcRrA5P-nCl38xE65nK-ICXzFhukDUvSHiQpYZotUG0g==> , "To exhibit its commitment to its privacy efforts, the industry must move its behavioral data collection privacy program to the phone, where more and more information is gathered every day." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010V9nSNfbz14f6c2KhKUc-jy4uNYnkcbHVqT9n39F9tpor03h7a3uSbVJCYcUcEM6LOA8-UosRhMIxTHXnOcoIV5Q-SDtmYxSsjueKzWHybUokQNF6cvDfWAPULJPtJAOsgrHSd5d2C4UpdV0Ly6Nb9hDt8PyTEFm25dWLfbsRhN8CrVPEkSsTzPMT4f2JKPIqJZwi1G3ciaSJ0FsvVp4SB4JL92cPPaJr1tLTqa1xqw=> 

 

Acqui-Apply

 

The MIT grads who formed the mobile/geo-location activity tracking startup Bahavio have decided to pack up the shop and join Google, Techcrunch's Frederic Lardinois reports. It's not an acqui-hire or an acquisition. The guys just decided to take a job with Google and quit their project. Behavio said in a release, "We believe that our digital experiences should be better connected with the way we experience the world, and we couldn't be happier to be able to continue building out our vision within Google." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010V9nSNfbz172ZXZheyXjgWnRPq2z2dhKPQD_Iev_TLmCUWLRZ6nxXy35SR0ruxgcdKV735NhsCkF71_bZJROEZDGBGG_5Z17OXXCiQVlMv7JsMQ-TVl35FSQKyLtzUzgp4Xo2V3TP64X-2ZGcVAut_YGJCAc3ErUr7c0SpgY3M3w4iL0HaUZpbm6_8MVScjoa56eyINlQodcJ4he5GU48CcRX6B2m1DpXqoPMqBmAOKdC2yDJNPkrwF3e196vuUP> .

 

Cro-mobile Man

 

Naveen Tewari, CEO at mobile ad network InMobi, tells Clickz's Matt Kapko how the evolution of the mobile experience will play out: "I would say creative is ahead, tracking is catching up, and targeting is something which the promise is very visible, but because of a few of these infrastructural pieces around common IDs, etc., there is still some distance to go." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010V9nSNfbz17I4WSLLHlhM0rJVnP9FIP08lQK7-BPANDwHO_1uWfvNCuEHinCoVKG-RYifx-F24nNSmIfxG_J1-Xy0o-RFb104qFE5PZPFirHtpwJrBKk6jwcHSo8BX-W_lEsOD_8FWTbKMVR6dhOhH6FClBQ1SiGFgzNYkCwZijOaRqe0L1YduaSPf-aaFKEQYitzozzGCtP7NNLDq5EHWRPMtHIqkfP> .
