I Am An Ad Network

 

Joe Mandese reveals the content of a recent fireside chat with Netmining CEO Chris Hansen on MediaPost. Mandese observes, "[Hansen] was crystal clear and incredibly simple in his description. 'We're an ad network,' he said candidly. That impressed me, because it's one of those things most ad tech players avoid comparing themselves to. I'm not sure exactly why, but the term 'ad network' has become a pejorative." Read more heresy <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010V9nSNfbz14u0iWxk6hutHzHb705LvBxJ8gBqw4tB9OHGGzwDsWnwJf_wHwVe75nkcHiL8QUsS7U9ahSmN77OYdIU62rJQvAhOqFJ28myEM-ziWYH1UH4Bskf0Blj11QprK8Cj4wAnAqDd0333N5uGAp9xCuuVeQNbhEuGrEa74Gza0QaBgyEZ38AVGHewlOYbv3hg8D9-0-82j-TGupI_8EKxqlDUzlDdoCwzRIhPY=> .

 

Billions Of Digital Pounds

 

Digital spend is on the upswing everywhere. The IAB in the UK chimes in on its region in a new report, "Just as digital spend crossed the £5 billion mark in 2012, mobile spend reached its own half billion pound milestone. Fuelled by smartphone ownership hitting almost two-thirds (64%) of the UK population in December 2012, mobile advertising grew like-for-like by 148% to £526.0 million in 2012 from £203.2 million in 2011." Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010V9nSNfbz16iJqXVhZE89IzR416fahF2ZV3lR4s2qSwd-t4lADHg9gpTqPBMYDK9U5PZAaLqRMhhPakk071Ap5Tv5IAIbrpoYUJ3rteSkLJVyohZ-rCAWk2X5TENIRowR3hIy-A7BaqGOBH-2pJGIvvabEv9-DipRQnXJZNtAaVC2OMlEm6vPS_WqKNEFmLf4WO3ZBG05wc=> .

 

Hiring Now

 

The U.S. tech industry is increasingly throwing its weight behind the immigration process, observes New York Times reporter Somini Sengupta, "Rarely has the industry been so single-mindedly focused on a national policy issue (...)," Sengupta writes. What companies want, he adds, is "a fast-track green card line for math and science graduates...no matter which country they come from, and a near doubling of the visas for temporary workers." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010V9nSNfbz14Q7fNTUUYyBMBRaiQvHVR8WkyJdMTKOYTIHVIofHBaci6cgzfrOPdPjuH4B_64IddpAxFprYFAExu8gZ4QKF6LrAZ-BB7SzU55x2wkXw9xgNTzLxQWQ6MgIr1AoTGVNxyvm2fawlN8kqb41o9KDqlOWvEgG7xKetuWj8jBpjyjp0DZgfthDB4TnbZUpJnMi5_51zBdpHjexTGUas4AUNbdskEydUNipbXq29A2w5rU_w==>

Mobile Intent Data

 

A survey released at the IAB's Mobile conference looking at how smartphone users interact with their finances (you did remember to file your taxes, didn't you?) finds that nearly two out of three respondents (58%) regularly use their bank's mobile app, while another 25% are aware of the app, but have yet to use it. What are they waiting for? "Most financial apps already contain rock-solid security, but consumers seem not to be as plugged into that fact," said Anna Bager, head of the IAB's mobile marketing center of excellence. And of course, more financial intent will be captured on mobile devices. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0015keV0WU_DI53IsgEwuqVq6q6Nfu5xRoai5nGOEjMhs772uPRjGGf6RAxKCoNdLqW_LhEkS_DdPx_3SZUdxKtFuSMOnyaMg27B9OiZmNFVJ_n1ygHJZJ5N3uGmt8VO5hqs9IbjgZz82WmIkZBJwS8bFjs4JnpmWh_ZZ_CIKB7711hXbaKy87Y0qnyItjCVvcWIJWAvAJtiK4_lBTBRL-THbocs7fbfq2dPAK6I0Q5RgOBUtqZKHYldPYTg47bD2bXD5DPX3oRPSs=> . Meanwhile, researcher IDC sees mobile ad momentum coming from brands. Read about it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0015keV0WU_DI5Jxt9rOZ2Ky8g74rcu-UeSYDyStXlujhN7k2MB4m0Pce1ckw0DZj-nkC9QQqHMFp5oh-vGPoEjdBNZHX5VxRuNPzWc6GDGF-0lkyJc8LktQyAiprC_FFy3QFAJSOys0RYg7Ob4YvyA1k6rLPYMOfnE14Z5RVT_jpL71yIyRZWczuD0SlOBulrF4y_8a3m8mwONR_QyPOBsU8UOZ3wg_Tn9iRBxsdiWeaw=> .

 

Programmatic Overhaul

 

Undertone's Eric Franchi calls for publishers to "clean up the clutter" in programmatic advertising on The Guardian. "This oversupply of ad inventory - fuelled by the programmatic era - is not only exceeding publishers' ability to sell, it is arguably leading digital advertising into a dark age," Franchi argues. One solution, according to Franchi, is to reduce the number of ads on pages and make the remaining ones bigger. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0015keV0WU_DI6sF5B7qqfqdm2aUl8DW6J-9tWEnX_le0WSga1toCjnbLZEeYBZtt2gP3W7wu07piJ2YLwYf774Y_iwkXOj-Ti-8U5ZlRbTyXLXtO3k7VJdJf_YZt1vsSKvCFiPYkjNcFRNZfKqDmYhKXB-pGYWfQsFd_DhkyQ_sQONzpEW3bsUteGcmXnQx9g9Qj0h4cclCZal0wbpHOyoVp-5YEZPP4AkdJWldKK66bEmyjuQQ36uqw==> 

 

Video Coupon Clips

 

Mobile coupons got a lot of attention two years ago, when the likes of Google and the Associated Press began producing virtual circulars for smartphones. But things quieted down as mobile ad spending continued along its fast, if diffuse, growth patterns. Now, the WSJ and Fox News, both News Corp. properties, are turning to mDialog to produce mobile video coupons as a way to build up rich media and smartphone placements. "It's an opportunity to fill inventory in a creative way," Jeff Misenti, chief digital officer for Fox News Digital, told Adweek's Christopher Heine. Read the rest <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0015keV0WU_DI4VBKmwPU__AIoiPUP8mCDC_tjIldJWlzSfWHHz4gHj1_9rIrqaGKSrC66yo79JuJLnmVwr7pT-2qJAA4dIR9YDHtY985d-DWdRcGXe3Bi_LIuR-jvMNtbWUsOl5l8Pr6s7WMJUiXM8N_EFqjMBzaMBFLVUaF4JJFWrZdQ8Fio0jdpmMq1Y7OvpaKHs4srko9k5GdAuvo4P9w==> .

 

Cookie Collapse?

 

In another story filed from AdExchanger's Programmatic IO <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0015keV0WU_DI5SN-rgoZQor9BvOCSzqw18st1XcgR4Dc-t8s-XAG-nKKeTLJX2snJMCCGK0474oikmESc3ESGf7OVP-OFDfxFKj85AKpAJ7T4jf_bTjZgsSA==>  conference this week, ClickZ's Susan Kuchinskas weighs in on the impact browser cookie-blocking policies could have on the online ad space. AppNexus CEO Brian O'Kelley isn't too worried about the collapse of retargeting should cookie-based behavioral tracking become more difficult, though he does acknowledge that buyers and sellers would take a hit. That said, he was understanding of the privacy impulse. "Retargeting might perform well, but it's creepy," O'Kelley said. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0015keV0WU_DI6XndZGxH5yIICmH1y9qkNe8qotY0CTKwWD6g4beyhAAqQu6ElHazTPpBcNKfizq2ZmNdAJQk8EhGfnLELDITelfBxfIhr1rMW0JOBzC8yrpzSQR_zN82A-TWVWPyZMDXIHBa_lA1apW7oMRDjRhbbfPKfbCRe4J-vmFTpsRUvean3OWNo7JeTfi3rwdasqU30=> .

 

Data Galore

 

People who use mobile IM/chat apps are 30% more likely to be interested in receiving ads on their phone, according to data pulled from a new Experian database. The Simmons Connect database contains a trove of behavioral information from 25,000 US adults who agreed to have measurement apps installed on their smartphones, tablets, and computers, as well as consumer data from TVs, radio, magazines, newspapers, gaming consoles, and MP3 players. Marketers and agencies can use the data to "understand with greater detail the behaviors of their custom-defined consumer target," Experian claims. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0015keV0WU_DI5DbgSx_daVTLizG2zNjisgkdYKzRcKZUB2CeM_tTEeShoXN3du983Rk9SZPgo5qbUDTU1NNW1rURITmStpB6UWSRyyyfka0TLaMhLIM5Vh0ciIZdg8RDZUxnxEDoGTDDTFPej3O7q2k1iECivJ3pQVpDRLh3WLjrqLWvK-UzYLzihFwuCEyb_3oKgwjl2OJraa-WxT5mdZeAZYBnkYk7TfOZ28N-VgwqA048U4mgMStNzT0I09m3KHAno0M5gou5rFPeWJ1S0kMA==> .

Backward Digital

 

Rubicon Project CEO Frank Addante follows up colleague Ed Carey's piece <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0015keV0WU_DI6j0VG-dW6Peh9tLoRq7O150IVJ5yAugnEKSPA1-BZgkAWl0krPYV8fb7wzJ1DxhuUjtzke2RtfktzxLFdexRc2TfEm7alpO9hbZ3OUQ5cEe6Wz3tCnWPgFgjiJCMPJXuDeAMJoJugEtHwoPoSrzlz1-8zTY5UuWFxVcNHYPpwvddWbLiNu1G5dV3MHuRCPmgc=>  on Programmatic Sales on AdExchanger with a piece of his own on digital ad sales in MediaPost. He writes, "To sell enterprise software, sales employees are trained to sell through channels. They do everything possible to enable the channel. (...) In digital advertising, we have it backwards." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0015keV0WU_DI7yK2jchNtLDdoQPVmy0ZOdom50bQgp3Q4DRPEGk-Os1KHZdRQN-WvtaJiZt5ROSJREHffgwQZwGZ7tqiPrXsfmLU6ze0KmBx1DYE8PBZssj0x8A-x1Dmmwg6dd3NayJLlPp8lInnGSLupmkX180kvk6ALeYo7S4JIqAADOdG4M4DcxQwsJLQJsH90J6LR9mVeDVzCiFQXd4ohMTOV6c2fAo4CNjrEaP7U=> .

The Trading Desk Conundrum

 

The party might be over for agency trading desks, writes AdWeek's Mike Shields as he examines the controversy surrounding the usefulness of independent trading desks. The debate, according to Shields, centers on "whether the agency holding company should decentralize its trading desk practices as programmatic ad buying grows in importance, or continue to house them in a stand-alone entity with its own profit and loss structure." More. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001f4YJG5RaL-dhZ2a_HF9i7Fl4Jgg4lzGjsC1Q6PmOLeMggsfXf3jO_VTwHSXbEMm_Z1EOWU--GR__YofbmjsO2uRi4rNPFlEf6zlXvzNZcTkuzPzY9Uh6ey6u_rYQiNPQn3HPIrG-VLtMzmdcrWkWT8ZHILIYQQWt04I-uLz5ALpt5k2-jXZgOHsMaClQnOkYQXc1pa0bBx9Q-Ogoxcz3DfM0CjZ4xY-STFICwb-q6AkjytG8vG9CVSWJPt0rBw8V5xQIt2iaXTk=> 

 

Social + In-Market

 

Facebook is adding new offline purchase data from Acxiom, Datalogix, and Epsilon. Advertisers can now target people who buy lots of frozen veggies, for instance, or children's cereal. They can pluck these segments from Facebook's self-serve interface, alongside its own social data. Read the blog post <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001f4YJG5RaL-euKJteUortaS64GJSPwEy8uSAOzIipH8w9JjjlSwNsNzBM3fpO_NN_R9ZBdULfA8NuUxYbYoOK1beEOyQLYdc_di4d2o43cJNr2k6IzHw7A2GkzgtJbtMYkDkn-YPvVaK2c1VqWraq6O1k2w4upL27wLnknZdGgCareW0V2waxBRiaRn8cAXdWLGXAjWTI4ZIjVHfio8NH4A==>  on the so-called "partner categories," along with obligatory privacy assurances. It's just the latest move in a sustained effort by Facebook to absorb the methods pioneered in traditional display over the past decade.

 

Video Ad Tussle

 

Do TV buyers care about online ads? Digiday's Jack Marshall looks at online video advertising and says, "There are (...) tensions on the agency side, of which sellers should be wary. Despite [Group M exec Ari] Bluman's comments, a tussle for 'ownership' of online video continues in some media-buying organizations. At some, online video has been taken away from digital buyers completely, and handed to a centralized 'video' buying team that handles TV, too." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001f4YJG5RaL-dUcukqY21hiTjJuYz_x0mh0Dqf3sBakKPYqqA19FRl1fQGlDRNZR_wKzxI8mZ4E5wXzPdh_wQgf1VJmBQUy9FJOBshhpLV3-kyC01CAmhLnfi9CVdpU3hob1FFxTj69teIWBY9h6dz_K552GRBL_XlBb58-2AFrrq7hcbDxwY0aQ==> 

 

Mysterious Ads

 

Ars Technica's Nate Anderson unravels the banner ad mystery in which ads showed up on high profile websites like Apple.com and Bing.com. "It suggested that companies felt free to operate as a 'man in the middle,'" writes Anderson, "one free to inject code of their own choosing into webpage requests that were-so users believed-simply between themselves and the websites they were trying to reach." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001f4YJG5RaL-dwvPf8Jivc8kSMf46-vdjzBlYMlztnnpBPfTDLInHIeXrF4-Odx5euFR94ZBuWqcgqux18WsxwT7pb3vGqfJzjQb5s1XKW9E41IJ9ExUKDMzfkEsFN_b-AEioskS7iobDPy-GUmov5u5-scch9-USFXayUayNr39arZqX8jeGT7zQb0E00Td8kpuFmBgSZhZQ=> .

 

Ad Tech Is Over

 

On Ad Age, Turn CEO Bill Demas says ad tech is over. Sort of. He writes in an op-ed, "Marketers have embraced technology. But they are demanding transparency, clarity and ROI, and instead what they often get from the industry is jargon and bickering over metrics and strategies. It's time we move beyond the ad-tech swordfight and get to a mature position where enterprise technology shapes the future of marketing." Voluntary Ads

 

PaidContent's Jeff John Roberts covers some comments Google ad chief Susan Wojicki made at Ad Tech this week. The gist: people should have a hand in the marketing content they see, whether in the context of search, video, or presumably, display. "We're moving to a model where the user is choosing to see the ads." She added 70% of YouTube videos are now TrueView, meaning the buyer only pays when the ad is viewed. More. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001f4YJG5RaL-cde6kBZ22UwHy0cVjNbpVUzDyIFcK9sY61oxn7wJ0SjEp2ZrcjO7Oa1HWVB-93EasEdZpCMuCddlTpPnKJ2xB345eTN0gzftP5SrHHZLFJtrQ8qXv5P3PCVpFAa_HBSF8MJnmUyZxfO2-cQLJCHp9XS5xVS9i9TISd_3XOLiL0gvDFhrQ6BMSwYRKNSmq6cGZJsB4n1slG1DSZwfVseHuIbUT4m4_c5e4=> 

 

Google: Phone Home?

 

BTIG analyst Rich Greenfield asks whether Google should try to put an end to Facebook Home, the social network's fullest <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001f4YJG5RaL-er9rVQ1Ue1g3BtaRAQdUJmMuqhsvGF0JZVwgkR1b_3ORvJPi9dbQgRbP6dGcJg1eyKwSbrK3l98LucJblZEaHqB1JmCJUlc-6RDGo2E00oAdLmOhw-64rHF_9aQJZR6wr22wsrLkgIQtVWfR6cXLid>  hardware integration currently available on the Android-powered HTC smartphone. Technically, he's not sure what Google could do to extinguish Facebook Home, but Greenfield does sense an incipient threat: While there is no advertising within the Facebook Home product today, we believe it is only a matter of time until it happens... If Google felt that Facebook spamming the Android home/lock screen with advertising is not in the best interests of Google/Android, why would it not try to stop these type of installs?" Read more (subscription) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001f4YJG5RaL-fE1MqQGuvR-UwXJfzhorz1KPh5A_RgGzruPTHMyjAHgzS_udSq7vu328Qz52TByEFs-jpfF4uvETioBpGVLfOE4xOUsV77_LiS7oipUzrl4_TgSndTtWbKNfbu4bnopW0BWItnSwTpk43xVtthwkROm-sn7IeNk65KN039CFwCvwcuCn7S6_6uFOPE7WELHNrPYimHncHUYxQPns-DSHxiYJVtcZ55F5U=> .

 

Yahoo Bids For Brody


Yahoo is trying to poach AOL's Ned Brody to a North America sales leadership role - or so little birds tell Kara Swisher. If true it's a surprise move, since Brody is not a traditional sales guy -- having been instrumental in building the AOL Networks (formerly Ad.com) platform strategy. Is Yahoo finally rising to the programmatic challenge? If so... it's legally complicated. "Because Brody has a 12-month, non-compete agreement with AOL that the Silicon Valley Internet giant, as part of the deal it is close to striking with him, will pay him to not work in that period." Swisher hears Brody may already have stepped down from AOL. More. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001f4YJG5RaL-fazGxG4nkaY0nsZxhRxEN-p6ZPcCBL_9t-zbqCNgzuSOlRfVJXziTkHXeSdCgHqQbqzvgr-0iXgjqiZJ1kZAUkYjrCpJEwwuv4BKF0xMsVFUSvq7uZUmcPjtfuhOrJtn7jKMNTvvqfaeV55YWvVuSiPiqo1POYKD_NmrjG-W72gLo826nxNHbSWH5v3D8pO1ZHuoj4xwKiLYHYIO9B_lt7lxprRnRd4CfyGvPVGZNtscmEcnNUR7pQ>

TripAdvisor Buys Gilt's Jetsetter

 

After a relatively quiet few years as the online travel space heated up around it, hotel and accommodations reviews site TripAdvisor has bought hotel bookings site Jetsetter from luxury deals purveyor Gilt Groupe, reports Skift's Dennis Schaal. Jetsetter will be folded into TripAdvisor's Smarter Travel Media group. The move comes a few weeks after TripAdvisor pleased analysts with the introduction <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001OQzmFQd60e_F4GEU-pRDgLLZ2NjtdytEL2fRxrTiQu7JAqcVSmEllWRsbCBmRHesf8aDRccuo8I29I0FSCjSCddPYvYPQFf9cPEGaYJ32_nl7-fpEGJpvCO2vSxg5oeJb1e_EkalWwDz7p5gh7unseQpChJUsyV0xg8ntXZT4cSOhqfa7nTNrobkZdrc1PPjytHGZunJSwHTZESfBCKF9WES3q3tiA82duTQHbSRuFeZD21BEacHI6UTjrnBVCmhthc0owjvxt8=>  of "meta display" into its hotel results as a way to create higher quality placements. "With Jetsetter and our own SniqueAway brand, we now have two leading travel private sale sites under one roof," TripAdvisor CEO Steve Kaufer said in a statement. Read the rest <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001OQzmFQd60e8MjM1z85CBrG1wkDq9FIBbQesVkt3o75BWwCccpiEijGpJu2h3yExnHHE_Eg48bm02EJRlSN0RNyDEeLIiwKL65RhfeSvuIvgXlZ6YZWPjxQBALHzcfPtLpUzson-zQbZNc8zcQXdBjEL7Eh6zqdmIRDZHBj3w1rw9uWsUAxMCdw==> .

 

Nice Weather For Mobile

 

A week after The Weather Company's big upfront presentation <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001OQzmFQd60e9mZgpO6MiT4uwUd68UwW9x-f7N777-f8fQTjlEf1erwSoiTxEyNEkK1i34ywh36UgifUrUuJslu1cEMa9Ier9A0ZP-aDYZOqswcGVIIMSudOyleeuQiGLdB21VbRsYkjV_qSkQ2-68p9ymr_gpsVPzgBPqPSWUUCPH5lQdDKhv1NgT8Q4RM4mnnluntaqUjOHLe9nxbblaAUpODY9NOrzlBp3LnBpGdto=>  to marketers and agencies, which included news of TWC's formal Twitter integration, comes word that brands like Ace and Taco Bell are interested in its mobile placements. "This is a new tactic for us," Eric Perko, associate media director at Digitas, Taco Bell's digital agency, told Adweek's Chris Heine. "For the right products, like food, it makes a ton of sense." Read the rest <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001OQzmFQd60e81DeIrD7_vM_hPSxP4qIiQxj9iXzDJ226Oj_GUT-rBSKK_32koDbwM6OesEahuHxZJ-_cN0wPI0ocv4dRUcND_o-P8_5w2uotJnMv4tX1HpMcoJeoDyKXwt5vESOX5mBqAWSANYjd3djcrYekQ0ierAlmpJdQH8Z3bW-8vxsGh7AoXPHnWabesqr-rh4zvf57sium-CWAe_w==> .

 

Ex-AdMeld CEO Barrett Gets Hooked

 

AllThingsD's Kara Swisher has been keeping up with the career of former AdMeld CEO and ex-Yahoo CRO Michael Barrett. Still biding his time on a permanent post since exiting <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001OQzmFQd60e9GzuiWj_ugPtekd9PA9AawUPGI6HAsZIuFPaHnTHP3Nhk8aQp3fvD-6FYVk_28mFLWNAJ7MsfvHmi_2tar47ZvY1SFnziISzTKqKP_immbSG-UNPhWURVINfnN-PLIukKgDF3iM1Rhr8Y0jM88_TX34YUEJaInJac=>  Yahoo last fall following the start of CEO Marissa Mayer's reign, Barrett has accepted a post on the board of performance marketer to online shoppers HookLogic. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001OQzmFQd60e8mHJ-yoaIz_7EzfHOTDmAKPNNwPj1ygc6hSo35gOKQQuLfipr4U9Xn6dRzYMJJWdS6YjHju-Wk3X-z9jCzHDATR25tJHLPMd5U7wAh9r2bv7h89twU4C584WekFo-gAoog6tO762TOfWoaj4lbWPsIAtX_dc7LN0VxpKSiKdUOrSOwH-6btLTTnO_4j1wwjAg=> .

 

Scroogled, Cont.

 

Microsoft's is once again using ad space to skewer Google's privacy policies. The Associated Press reports on a third wave of ads that "depict Google as a duplicitous company more interested in increasing profits and power than protecting people's privacy and providing unbiased search results." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001OQzmFQd60e9keBgFVnfxpoXdTGjoDdNr61nZmBHDvdqEmiB0bFeZkOI4uiqVqF3Co6ohKm0oOo45ePhXLuOXyHHo4aVV_khv5DMPLfFrHozdll79kK_jdSKewL0iMKu0i0W9Ppul8JMR2f-GMCo-f851IwWe9A9jYI2mH-vbzhwftw6azecUkdRN247tMu9dGLjIEOpdIuo=>  The consistency of messaging around privacy almost begs the question, is Microsoft's Do Not Track stance part of a marketing strategy? Paranoid... right?

 

One Day, $1 Million Spent On Facebook

 

Faced with the formidable task of acquiring 500K Facebook fans in a day on behalf of one client, Nanigans used every play in the book to extend reach. In a blog post dealing the effort, Director of Campaign Management Carly Rodgers <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001OQzmFQd60e9KarW6k-pdbtI0r0tkRRQqXHlEeyAHw9dHz7Pv6aPSNrmuD59rEiJ9Vl_-uZUq0uBYjg28_0dZcGks-5ej-w5vO6qIQtR64x8GTuWGcGdT_S9QotMYbpBnBSXELpi7gRmZNNYAI5bbuZJL8VOWgN68>  says, "The campaign's location parameters were extended so that it had active ads running in every country on the map. If there was translated ad copy available, it was used where it made the most sense... we split up the task of creating new ad plans for each language and matching the appropriate languages to each country." The grand conclusion: "It is possible to efficiently spend one million dollars a day on Facebook advertising." More. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001OQzmFQd60e8kP92iB9ap7TIJiycp0c4-JgzYjVRBr3_vr0cNTcAcJ4QHOvdYz7_0WKPm7KKOfEABbkPqK2mvg5D-_OlPvjNQzCKZtWl3i7MeNUbkA48KZIMLXDVrSk378fWstWdaduKntBpdWQvPwFczJryt-OwzC84xPYK5WppRn914WT5X-tFasEPIupSRx4coPSN4oQz2mYOiwfYg_A==>

Slow Programmatic

 

Yesterday at AdExchanger's Programmatic I/O conference, eBay's head of digital display said programmatic needs to be less about real-time. As reported by Forbes' Robert Hof, Stephen Howard-Sarin said, "The marketer needs to know, how long does it take for someone to buy a product? That period of time obviously changes between a cup of coffee and a car. In programmatic, we tend to narrow that to the next few milliseconds. We need to move people along during the entire span." More. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001EQfsaLxnqoJYILdNIdxN7heB3zqjAHw_VDSouS14zFDxH7QqixSxm-bQWdn6OtVyt-3Y4PmGbGG3dyNnc0S9dmErE7gys0Ak5sVEkNyrIYxHNNzmER1NNQ9BmbhZKwnlKtc1NAEUkFV023f1DItp41Hh7ZcIMn75jRt3qM_foqHF4q53Il0QYXp78imy1TaIcprHisi6d6ERjxBwpTsEzvusVHAyJ-KGUNjXxymN_dI=>  Forbes also covered the "cookie armageddon" angle from Programmatic I/O. Read that. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001EQfsaLxnqoKPH0WAPHjkorNtTkpPDSOjfuz3x7pZ5FldN6RpTxlErNc97LYz9_y6n-M1V0r4YxkdpCYdgvAQqOU_nobE9U1tRVqxI1ffOtVL_LsZzHqJmL7q-Q_M50LXWmROe6NSQ9uLTflud6ONrCgFs95geNB_T1bBaSMf77gVbxEHRAFfY93LzTT4IQLX7xvSunO7V9Le0BmS58hIwFo1NAIhNW8kVCzSp018L3KREUvvkI6w01Ej2CrztX85> 

 

Video RTB Rises

 

Forrester Research forecasts RTB spend for online video ads will reach $1.14 billion by 2014, in a study commissioned by SpotXchange, making up 24.7% of US online video ad spend that year. Forrester used its online video ad spend forecasts, along with interviews with online video buyers, sellers, and publishers, to calculate its video RTB forecast. The study highlights how online video is supplementing traditional TV campaigns and how programmatic buying mechanisms will not only grow, but also diversify. The bad news, notes <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001EQfsaLxnqoIAfvCx6zgycO2yIM9UigP5_ilomDwseA_BtV626WJZAxbgxht3HMLLrspGVQy5dkm5cV0F06-f4AdgZXy3IvR1a08EUVUToy7rf9gV1rIpYnBTwNDpRWYv1O7eb8nCO7dP34FmVe0FzFWSxUS60_oxN8i2HpHxePkP4MrFn0iw6tZQYEeIl6f98ljAzOE6t2AsEk5lXnHFTTqyE78RLm73MYXHhX9CfXiHMJwm3OMW1g==>  Paid Content's Jeff John Roberts, is that video ad prices are under pressure. "The word is out about video's promise," Roberts writes, "and more and more people are showing up to grab a slice of the pie." Read Forrester's press release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001EQfsaLxnqoLKHOTF0y9arX1n3ksJeO_TGwAiB5U4tI-i-FvXcBlsTtd14msGDfmxxA54S_sOJ0XaL3s_Aaw1HKalqCrYZv9BzoTz660a2FYMwdeocXFUNhaQGa1jpReZL8FyNX4pJWUGfb1hrVF3vUnjt4FRe9qBSfqEoWZd_4zg4cohPtWlEKSWVevctV4gWuck5lo-WcANrbcdIQhMWDFmQq-ASbianNueUjLnjKEmZ--EogmqqdPZtAK-QZOFqpbT2n-hGIAjik0dqCljHwJyBihtLd3ANf4uv54ElCk=> .

 

Yahoo's Albatross

 

The New York Times' Jenna Wortham and Nicole Perlroth lay out the challenges Marissa Mayer must overcome to inject fresh startup blood into Yahoo. "If you are a quality start-up, Yahoo is still not the place to be," Colin Gillis, an Internet analyst at BGC Partners, tells The New York Times. "It's hardly your first pick." More. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001EQfsaLxnqoItlR1FxasLOs7uuGlgAI0-LenE6Zf-IpUcuhX4To67mzddyIothoihLJC6Lp7x9g7_kpbWohAvKuohJ3GNhgnVuDRTLpIg3YNCSGY-wrQKAmiK9nN9Lp5p7VIK9qSYrU8FoeAONQ3o65z15p2W7CmGDhW_2IghtaCLIvUuZPlL_iWx5LmEHRVkTGy968KGi_5TQBZFdzFGIzAXzm2rBmQm6xCxRlV7kGosuJ6GSSNV_Q==> 

 

OpenX Gets Holistic

 

Making use of its 2012 acquisition <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001EQfsaLxnqoI7rnsBMBwZqkRlU_aj3y2-z57MrdQy2fV53tF2flsTN0YTW1jriI3QV6gY-pnzakeotmm35BJsliTPCIy4ShRsFCRdbCcieDP1YoemyVvUNSpsyI5aW2GOJR83Ry6wl7Ux5XuLWUmXN34ODWtM13cnlnnz5xsY7jQkjCOreGpbQiAoj0qd1QBT2I71bUdhUzxynjBlwyxzCwuAgBbhSJXZCfqJkfVrlIXOySJ4h__qZejPztGldMHE>  of digital content analyzer JumpTime, OpenX added a new sell-side service called Revenue Intelligence. It combines content and ad monetization to maximize yield. JumpTime co-founder Anke Audenaert leads the team. "OpenX is able to leverage the power of its ad monetization data with the data from its content optimization products to maximize publisher revenue in a way that has never been done before," said CEO Tim Cadogan. More <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001EQfsaLxnqoLSIES2mJz5m-Igf0tH27Ga1yCfiaYhHRLgXpdZPOU1O_Fq0y0jTQbro59f8Ls7ZfoWjCOszKYRb6WVrITDB6CXVOGI6FKn-7QrZvf-8DtmiqOS0lJcElWdu01xJQ-G7Ra12SY2lWQyXA==> .

 

More Money, Less Problems

 

Media consultant and blogger Dorian Benkoil takes a look at how the programmatic space is dealing with fraud and privacy issues these days. He's noticed signs of progress. And that progress can be measured in dollar flows. "It's a sure bet that the predictions of increased dollars flowing through exchanges are correct, and that more sophisticated technologies will emerge," Benkoil writes on PBS' MediaShift. Read the rest <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001EQfsaLxnqoJ7KJQaXuXF6zsbhT-7mQogoK7LuVxqS3xb68tPz-pkICq9XP2hPCyv7TqdmpkCtczn_DWsyF9WyrOczh0weMt8N46aHEXSMK3-nlqqjw3WKQzGUYxZSqWXCvdsCRBH44RrvoGZ7lxK85wI5aIUqoC20S4yX-Zh9JjDp8feWI8GSQCZynuMGRvkYnCWMKpxW6zuDdOo9SlC-5VPE-VvAtYvCWbFyq54zeyBfQ26IMoplw==> .

 News Round-Up <http://ih.constantcontact.com/fs116/1102602719219/img/94.jpg>   

Here's today's AdExchanger news round-up... Want it by email?
Sign-up here <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0016lrV6NoQ30gPJaZPq1xhEP6rj9AnMXm6fsITG3hXupxv84KuTI8EKLiJ0y6swg-J0Rl838NzRbyvAlZ3IdYJPqVyccbJRrY14VTMx0WbeNoOywAjAv2NZ3QhnVGC4WqHWTzpg2MZj8A=> .

 

Adapting To Nielsen OCR

 

Adap.tv has signed on to use Nielsen's Online Campaign Ratings, which aims to measure the reach of video ad campaigns across screens. The video ad platform hopes to show it can tackle issues of price, quality/engagement and above all, a clear set of measurements. But will it kill or enhance the GRP? Judging from what Adap.tv is saying, it's hoping for the latter as it launches the offering in the UK. "The key to driving widespread adoption of online video is to ensure that digital can speak a language to which TV buyers can relate," says Adap.tv's Brian Fitzpatrick in a release. Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0016lrV6NoQ30gPqVVhQtsPMgoj7EXBmFizLQBAPbrsJ5PmVSb7yqUaFO6v9JIWAOksEIm1on53EvLHqjnxYZKRFaniKtKU0-CssAdtMrX-9AjO6QNN0w9awcitVpOma7JT> .

 

Attention-Getting

 

Celtra, a rich media mobile ad server and analytics provider, says its AdCreator software now incorporates enhanced video reporting. "Advertisers are keen to know which parts of their videos are the most interesting to viewers and conversely, where any drop-off happens," said Matevz Klanjsek, Co-Founder and Chief Product Officer of Celtra. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0016lrV6NoQ30gLxw63TN7-nGcRIhKUyBNQhBgyPT0Dbxw8Tc6YOJJjzneAl7XfXCYvEcu0WozGW3TgqoiVHxT23jYn5iaFgFbsEA7V_3-ngJ6STfTlxdFyKiklXISr7Gha_Ut76CvHQ2k_DCUy53gshbo1LqmRVb4jxv5Mtish8k6hNGTYPaX4D3GAOw1ToGbH8RAQPkDg6lhK50QSVHFiH8UqnFyx9DWE> .

 

Data for Everyone

 

Visual Revenue, a predictive analytics platform for news editors, makes a case for why audience data is just as essential for editors as it is for advertisers. "Advertisers have long since...bought into data," writes Visual Revenue's Rich Ullman in a blog post "and they are using it so aggressively through exchanges and programmatic buying that they are squeezing every last ounce from publishers. This imbalance must be addressed, and it can only happen with a combination of data-driven thinking and distinctive editorial voices." More. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0016lrV6NoQ30hrQoXhcIksZs-MWjgmnxZCAmvOG4ke6FFHlko8AKPXScZW562ylhMzNB9Qhi78EV4z7xDe-EtHgaPUg8ce8RB25LPKrLtkGKGn84FXNeArTBTO6U8mrJbNpLKp8jaAJtQKp0isR_GPJJwQ19qhW-xetauySZE2lkrIbd0KU8JFJF0307AsvHvtkpTW_WrQ-kvIS-O79bZloO8vNtcNZYob> 

 

The Neal Mohan Story

 

In a feature article on Business Insider, Nicholas Carlson recounts Neal Mohan's rise to the Google display ad management throne. Carlson says that Mohan has had offers from competitors to run their companies, but still he remains firmly at the GOOG. Invite Media (acquired by Google in 2010 <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0016lrV6NoQ30idyFPTeRGfWuQAPfUc-CH5WgMI-3oLmHW0JJhn8S1rJlTKPscgN5BSrCAEJkih2f87sgG7QGPt124tFhY1-nLEEKqpghYucf2RSRdHmLz-g7QSFYytZozxL97-jxdZYSSpZJerpfxiiNdkAPp-NbUmx2tnxOxD9jE=> ) founder Nat Turner reasons why: "If he had another display guy above him, or if there were political nonsense going on, he would probably take off sooner. But there isn't." He's the chief. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0016lrV6NoQ30ivd2EIX0xBJPanPuVF7fPlI0Zw__K88FV7LatJ_PEhTs7HXo5wLi3h3136HiGRMiflD84pB5rHnAHdaUg2DFW9Snl8Mve8t3qFBxdqdKj3NUk-QS4XBclxSDeOBBrm0wATBPsYXnrhD2qOdf2TT6lfQ0O6hMkUt1SuS9x7DfO5ZQ==> 

 

Cross-Device Opt-Outs

 

Drawbridge is one of the more buzzed about vendors in the cross-device data collection space (along with Adelphic Mobile, TapAd, and AdTruth). The company last week set up a deal to support tracking opt-outs through TRUSTe's mobile ad privacy program. Press release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0016lrV6NoQ30h29FpyRJyDQjkAVPPVv0wG8mkUbgbi7rFQ-rFrbMK47OfITaHXEV9_0ID5_uw7Ppn-XkWsOOr0yyQQ7eQ_ggDn8LvdjBDsjNdkAY5bBW2L9933DPmit70nSSNjzWf59mkx1DlsPERMPXdVJLK6XvWT> . Drawbridge CEO Kamakshi Sivaramakrishnancited TRUSTe's compliance with the EU Safe Harbor standard as a reason for the pairing. Global privacy compliance is "key to our global client business" she said in a statement. The question remains, will regulators and privacy advocates accept industry-administered privacy systems for so-called device "fingerprinting" technology?

Retargeting Exposed

 

IMedia's Dax Hamman takes site retargeting apart to show that it is "there to plug the leaks from our marketing funnels, and stick a Band-Aid on what is broken." Marketers, Hamman continues, need to "understand what [site retargeting] really is, find a smarter way to measure it, and break your reliance for it." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0016lrV6NoQ30gCCkNuZC5e_NJ7paMfx8ZOaQyVoUdBCQJxCi8erTsHzm-WN9Z4UolHp2y9Dr10sgdm68Jl-MaLDAhCkq71T2rrFU2JIM40WDwmrPT_GbWzmUeD7Ut9yJ206zSZ-khpI26YgAiHv3in9w==>  In other words, site retargeting benefits from all those years of marketing spend and brand building. Measure accordingly.

Measuring 'Walk-Throughs'

 

PlaceIQ is offering a new metric for mobile ads that's essentially a real-world equivalent of the online "view-through." The so-called "Place Visit Rate" is defined thusly: "The ratio of people who viewed mobile ads for a physical retailer and subsequently were observed in that store." Blog post. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001yZ7ou1f5l8ghSTEKbVLbYsNAveQF-Rh4GFMtQoA3xJnSsGC1xEmzokPjhJ3ZlM9S3o68Kx-TAq1jOMWOT3kJFmxAKclGW25ms_yyeynz3Y0jRKL9f4aXWZfBf1Gfk6adGzo5Bp0SDp-Z80FZjLVrc_w1tm3KoJUwJaJleL6ZwFUgNTmGIpAy_w==>  AdAge notes that Starcom MediaVest Group is offering it to retail clients. More. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001yZ7ou1f5l8iCWgPVvppg5PTiJDEQ21H1vAYiUtUUQmVQGShxEkCUPCd_2B57xzCYkKvTFNlCFU3O9aJbSrtv-tsoO422Zg-XjGXW4LFZ_oT59GvGpoen8EbG4SMd03lZMr1rFvxtt8_ZZWvoj53Luxoq9GaE1Jc58SKkHtML8Smjktq1iOCsHpvxCvtDyvjNVoRKZtSjnbk=> 

 

The Multichannel Challenge

 

The good news is internet traffic from smart TVs and set top boxes is rising alongside traffic from tablets and smartphones. The bad news is companies must work even harder to reach consumers, reports Broadband TV News, which cites findings from the Netbiscuits quarterly web trends report. "This evidence creates a serious challenge for brands, as more devices come in numerous different technologies, sizes and configurations. Without adopting a fully future-proofed multi-channel approach, companies risk falling behind and ultimately wasting money and losing consumers," said Netbiscuits CEO Michael Neidhoefer. More. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001yZ7ou1f5l8iaKkJN0A9kFgtrE_byAwN8ov87kZz2W8iEQkkM1FefD-1asaNE1sF3vrGzFtBbs9VsVzSnSxFIBB0J9AHIv2vs04Q1y1_JL1hiee6TYhJMFwc-l8J6QLjlvi2D7o5jhm631bX4DgrWi94Pb9SC5wWykFvac5KPPB_2i7kfy9_gJ6IZ2pprrlYE> 

 

Google Misbehaving

 

Google is once again on the privacy hot seat-this time for failing to meet requests by taskforces in France, Germany, Italy, the Netherlands, Spain, and the United Kingdom to modify its privacy policy. The result, observes All Things D's <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001yZ7ou1f5l8hORz3RbbTl9Fw5w18J61cHCYz6zmTx_6PJE7SMjYgT6ccAJ7tnwlWhv6B5-JXXrFjB3sd3DjWnb3mlbLpESLkSsI3TILxCnnplzQVhj1GLqR5LG41mj-ER7Owf-ibqgiZksD-aDClQ5wTN6H-E4cI17qxF_-jBjHJ9QqqrjqhZGJEd8c_DgdxvOH8DoL3BIl4Tuht4bzBAHQ==>  Liz Gannes is "additional investigations and inspections by the Europeans, but this time they're being called 'enforcement actions' and they're being conducted by each country individually." Over at the Verge, Aaron Souppouris notes <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001yZ7ou1f5l8jjYyF48w8qzqvKYrbw-0O967jwynosr9D80zuPUnog6tUxxPOKNbGvOAQA8Q9LO2-Zsf5CALk-GzATNZ09foPiWSg6j15Hrmq3YY3oyfHdv7eqYIZiAR_oICvgRBjMxIfzmOb3kMVzLqKDHG8W_lTfkKuHxeZQRlE97rVbuUoMN3qrmk4GLHpU8iz3V74Vt-J3OW4fix-_4kCHczDZ2ZsK>  that Google could face fines levied by each country. Read the CNIL's press release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001yZ7ou1f5l8iDbUgunCeiWPYwTSWuvsNiRQYNOjcp0h1WOLMrEj4co4FpC-wgf-dNit2bXUFt6S0w7Dc-PcC_rHkifttrBDEvVuXEr8bz1H559b-f1gTlAs5FC5ENR8zAbvsIAIs4isrGuq4KKNi-RpfJ2ds06qNX107W1umLd9RtMFg_gwzWqXpr0nZfdseBAklJM9HQTdCry6oeRCVVz4aeJLxRz5sbFuRhof9NbCsvp2CUCqJSauSYnKuLT83Q9PyuaLF7YkyHAACKDfBNgARnc1sVzH3ga3NYH8Md-wRWxiwb80NyQw==> .

 

Local Yokel

 

Are there fumes left to burn in the local ad network gas tank? Local.com apparently thinks so, having launched a new "premium" network of newspaper sites and other locally focused properties to capture national ad spend. Greg Sterling notes on his Screenwerk blog, "This is almost exactly the same value proposition of the former Real Cities, which was owned by McClatchy, Gannett and Tribune Co. and was one of the first attempts at a national-local premium ad network." Centro bought and eventually shut down Real Cities. Unrelated but related: the sails also seem to have gone slack in Yahoo's Newspaper Consortium. More. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001yZ7ou1f5l8jskOsBhysmX_OHEjQ8MeAfbAAx9I3MXI3ErDl2RLH56K4orayjCyb0ls_Z5eHn1GxQ5t0n65v7Tzav_6VCptw9K90oHjr_wa8bwZsNZTTCvG4XbBaMGMQYSTy5AVZFYvC2PgE-FQgQLGQettMAIoFxbRYMtkvVw3zNq8Mkao9EZtOYXtlgdW8WTRSoGyi9Xq-4vHwXQJ1EXA==> 

 

NYT Friendly Takeover

 

The NYTimes.com has long been trumpeting its custom homepage ads as a solution to the problem of attracting brand advertising akin to the expensive ads in its daily newspaper and weekly Sunday magazine. The latest is a front-page ad takeover for insurer Prudential that lets users see an image of NYT front page of the day they were born, which caught the eye of Adweek's Lucia Moses. "While the Times has been praised for taking an innovative approach to advertising-especially for such a traditional publication-these kinds of initiatives may well invite backlash from editorial purists who would bristle at the mingling of editorial and advertising," she opines. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001yZ7ou1f5l8gU7wRfYDdlwSA6xNhsCBFahZofkv38ItgBF_QSMxaZI3HyW3boRAgqHZGQn3qXqJeTGUWhUJCS8JncFCyewKBT3t3qBFsBFo4ncKfIH9V0xNtHOAtBERrWLHdVMjS8Jkf_pL8ahiC7DmeJ0OCAenxf71kABFmciNBqDfTI5QpeQln_hEk7XOHzxMtHO6--AvOjGfl1ZuY4an29gmkRkvg_> . Interestingly, the image can be shared on Twitter and LinkedIn, but not Facebook.

SinglePlatform Gets Yelped

 

Unlike politics, all online advertising isn't local, but proximity is important for certain publishers. Take reviews site Yelp, for example, which has signed on with business listings publisher network -- and Constant Contact acquisition -- SinglePlatform. "We didn't feel like we were quite ready yet with our publisher network, and our business wasn't quite ready to scale," Wiley Cerilli, SP's founder and now-VP at Constant Contact, told Street Fight's Steven Jacobs. "But you're going to start to see a lot more combined marketing efforts from the two companies." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001yZ7ou1f5l8gjQE7JjQx7jtYmZ48QvcjNBbubNc6B4B2w3DBHb8ILhOTgR4yPd7di9SR_xszNu5dGVhAdsKAnW0p0fuCkfiGWhvKMUA5AQ_wSRzVSiDZTx4qQvbfAuv94wxJ-Q0TKO0GVdsZ_4h65DC-qH2hjYNhyITiv3iFtlssbcrAk7fSdz-kOAlEDkiNXpLOt-s9JAOXKgGhZNFNKI4lZtrZHRHQjJvkDi738RAZZdMhqtUVvDGGkahpfCdZ0> .

 

Stop Going Native

 

The Drift's Doug Weaver has already said it's time for the ad industry to eschew <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001yZ7ou1f5l8hwDZqH_5_Q1GYs4e1Hxee2_3nBB19hNsc7wE8XS3hv5H2z_4Hj_2jxO7N-PpUhWCrQV7Xvd-jYWsRCAuYOzkVI3gZQVqYgAAVFdNPbdcawuR9ccDuvfAmp8KyiruPQNHi6aCxy2kEd1Q==>  the term "programmatic." Now, he thinks it's time to clean house and stop using the term "native advertising" as well. "Everything from 'product placement' to sponsored tweets to 'anything that's not a banner' has been unceremoniously dumped in the Native Advertising hopper... Yes, it's definitely time to click on 'Empty Native Advertising Bin' and start over," Weaver writes. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001yZ7ou1f5l8hib3LBUppiOrLhSvebDq0xlCUHot8rHBFi50mzGeAd8LnnhnAvKrjCjP4rnzj4QtRbFEQiHSgMxUURSWW6HLnKvF9dImmMGYGArB3nMETrjam6YhqpeejFQdL7T3bEG5rch-jfkUNL6TwMZ4kJvBbR> .

Commerce Adding Offline To Online

 

J.P. Morgan analyst Doug Anmuth shares his notes about eBay's recent analyst day. He calls eBay "the next generation of commerce featuring the convergence of online and offline shopping, and significant impact from mobile devices." More notes (PDF) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001i_yYjQgN0dmiom9hxDtHu-A-z93emvfg7r5S-bbfIz8glkVdFhBljnfoqj-HOkzCfHsVtvi0z9xsiOy_jDDmO6FD_NGN30N7QbrfBon0xMGspMITNii4ah2VHjMdjJz7pFMcYmrg3EVRAELKI7Yew2F0FdrjQOT1FBTR7kQkPz4TAvkPyTiXI6oRwJBSs_2h> . Jefferies analyst offers his own thoughts: "eBay is ready for the age of omnichannel commerce. eBay management believes the transition is already underway towards a world where mobile is expanding commerce beyond conventional stores and eCommerce websites." Read that note. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001i_yYjQgN0dlzCh9TN3QPD7X5XFmXHSYFjAN3hpJI-Rm0ltsJoSeUtbpVVb8YrVrC61IkZtabA8TK-Hu9jh1NMU1aWy9BOFKzzjJyriNhZD02UkohL6YMrSmsi_j6E_wpHfxQf4dx5Bk=>  The media in and around commerce will be infused with online/offline attribution data, too. And the new eBay Commerce Network should help (was Shopping.com). Read about it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001i_yYjQgN0dnuPoGD8gZSkjHMkvhEjlcSKt7pzyB5JgMFPcdjBJBqpvVWqOARKvpGfG8GYKSN0cZ0JXAnY5ehggMCl-g3kfiQmy6H59tIKTmHpFrE6jb60NmPtm9pzEbJSq2PY5bERL971GP1djx8IpllhyaD3fZu8Y-dJAffxaqNP5BDeW6ln62GaTlyuM4O673xkNyhf64_nKLH9-gwwA==> 

 

About-Face for Facebook?

 

AdAge's Cotton Delo wonders if Facebook's willingness to push News Feed ad inventory into Facebook Exchange means it is sacrificing its high ideals. "Social context is now an ingredient in Facebook's marketing recipe instead of being the whole meal." Delo writes. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001i_yYjQgN0dnqBxTdfHYTHxRcAivwKEQfItLjNpVRAUKE_swFuEJNH6LLzhu9SpkMOAgrEV8dXbQ3WX2vKwYOjuen-kplrTow9-tor4rsjPjY-DfhWKAF6ea4QpSeVni4HQDz_qumb6T5LJ9D3O5BfdXsjLCyLRsPfTOnIiQrijDfDvbyCOrJorzxxFswf80H>  Meanwhile, the Facebook Engineering team introduces "Link Bench" as FB intern Tim Armstrong (you can't make this up) says, "[Link Bench] allows us to simulate the load generated by subsets of the social graph, which is important when evaluating database configurations tailored to specific association types." There's a lot more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001i_yYjQgN0dkJ43dpqG_BIakqIMAIMFH7pVDwNo_7z-1Kjjf4x7oG6SE8EUW_VdI3CRIn-j8uQSqB80xAewPdx0ErsdsVwDVZdF4-BuIUh3IwktaQcSnM8-L7X1lUcO5lwQSF5JM_Tu-wgANSj4bavhadPDHuCwk7HoeQ-r4950gZ9NJVDuym7yOMM6YP6Dgo02FvJ_VQNbteVfnEv1z47tWGGvFm-9k33FklxReUBCuoiSPJ_1FiFzOug41qG7L7> .

 

The Do-It-All E-Commerce Brand

 

More online retailers are bringing the supply chain in-house, morphing into manufacturing and distribution giants. New York Times examines the trend, noting some brands zig where others zag. "In some cases, the online brands are choosing not to discount, keeping the extra profits from cutting out the middlemen for themselves." The marketing implications only grow as browsing and purchase data increasingly inform areas like R&D and pricing. More. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001i_yYjQgN0dmz0_SqetvRJhC9u5iRZE4DDcx47KTlA55d_K0pCbCur-UAELvzXs0XU5Whqm9BjdM71tgeSCWSLHvZB_g0qf9N_q4Yn7ux-g4qQAkimuARELmwwYfN31GCHnYgKKM1lATkuCY9TaVeuo2a0-4HOav_dRQ0vtoulQbRdBlAx2xj5JxGsm7pfdr1LfuCm-fX4X-nbLbY7ymqqRpry_BRLIISb48_gClEnL3rYd7h1KCM24jsHNrmoWf8jjK1itB0qmc=> 

 

Patents And Mobile Targeting

 

On MediaPost, Laurie Sullivan covers patents that she says were approved by the U.S. Patent Office for Yahoo recently. Is it the mobile Yahoo future <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001i_yYjQgN0dmvsHllft1m65qgb99Ix5w7rlDxx2uXBeBtuYokR8cqUevZKxY4xNqS2jHAzBbabonc7i466KMwDqSnHQ8mk8xhTkWeHEuWEKlBf21gw9X4zqphDbAD35gHav1nljaElonQzdZ-fpCfuYewVRS0Y1jO6zCt4mzgAWc=>  that CEO Marissa Mayer seems to be collecting startups for? Sullivan writes, "The Yahoo patents point to a mobile authentication framework that ties in desktop content and searches; cluster cookies for identifying unique mobile devices." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001i_yYjQgN0dnxb-MBZCSUpt853vbh1UFrNFykBht1AVcNBUmo0qxYzQAUqbmj9Uk4cKfE9G855G3cmqkLddSnJGowVvLtYIv17wnA9GldqcU-Jh62EcIYd7b-YddenKzfR1CoO1P2lwbByIKOVh9mSNv-PWXoQWUmdH2CZ8168Xysc-m8LPs1R7IbsstocsxD8Y-TVDwEHwMNCKDoTqK62f-6GHZTU7J3O-0fbdekXVg=> . And, see it on USPTO's website. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001i_yYjQgN0dltp9sbH1ugPUmTrPySggVjH7yUp-LvbOMgA2692MpSfrp0pcUDQr29NGudSQGobhpvPUi0xiHLMbiDAWllveHWNlKzgbT1wtaTe19fsLfYPZInKiEwxZoWUJoopa1zOWm0xMj6itPxfLgzexR7q3XF7l6zZg2TOlNf83tFZ8wWwEKZvPRWyUEI-E-W3NxfoGK5-I9tp1-dsflciFkISlS60TVBYZlZWpQzU7ddA0bdN6c5YlcjUdO0ZyBbzDidSpH5JmM1RfgU15bBj9kJ39hoSxkmO4Y2bRgKXclQGKzcuubVRSWxOXpAlDD-lTFZiL9hoWLuJWewtoc6y7HYqwhMCaQv020igVfUISPLtdYMIob2yG8v3X2znQPaz4DXw0Y6nEa5DWsFfsd92C1tw_UUYA29xIU58hTQNsxl2r0GPcrmjr5zpoZInpcF0VteM7g=>  This sounds like a way many companies will use their first-party data to effect ad targeting. Which begs the question - if these patents are that broad, would Yahoo enforce them?

 

Premium, Publishers, Programmatic...

 

Ever since private marketplaces/private exchanges arrived on the programmatic scene two years ago as a way for publishers to feel more comfortable about real-time bidding, there's been a lot of speculation about their value. But some buyers approve of the model, suggesting they're seeing the benefits as well. "Premium publishers should go about their monetization strategy through a combination of private marketplace and programmatic reserve," said Brian Lesser, CEO of WPP's agency trading desk Xaxis, tells Adweek's Tim Peterson. "We're not going to encourage a premium publisher to participate in open exchanges because it devalues the inventory and doesn't provide control of what advertisers go up against their content." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001i_yYjQgN0dn3UNo8J15FIy830NtCKRmqhaBmTuC6K3rYYWj47UDbI6nI9GMSqg_M6Ye5CGPPmSpauBsEh8KZ-o8k8p-okqCYqcnb4U360qc3bSi_kAAOvwnjTD5yovBqqPl_B8kTXDmt3dRasPB92agGXmUUJluiH8hgK7ieHxkSKSO0wEW0Fy14A2Zvmf7G2QeXpGS0NQuWXnZTX4pJ0jZm4SqmgbNX> .

Phablets Are a 'Phad'

 

There's no point trying to walk the middle ground sometimes, particularly if you're a device whose description falls between a tablet and a smartphone. Mobile analytics provider Flurry looks at usage and finds that "phablets," as it calls these in-betweens (Samsung's Galaxy Note is the chief example), hardly registers when it comes to app usage. "The 'Is it a phone or is it a tablet' devices otherwise known as phablets have attracted interest, but currently command a relatively small share (2%) of the device installed base, and their share of active users and sessions is also relatively small," Flurry's report says. Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001i_yYjQgN0dnPqVH5_YZwXWfXhnyam3ZA9213_u3xFGcceha5uklQNqXgb6H4JSt_zAbWHBnM5xiqvkC_O89gFi_ZeZxsEf0d6YF8fxehUf1CpqvrmEcN48v1lPLm2vy27h7jcZt0LSOh2TyfWGUXMGTyhMj-NXb_TpSeZo9LGlq07lIJgmO1cwu5IWydl0nnzZMEZc828vQ=> .

 

The Facebook Phone

 

On the desktop Internet, Facebook has been called "a better cookie." If the company is close to launching its own phone, as reports indicate, it begs the question what advantage (targeting or otherwise) does "owning the smartphone" create? There may be potential to renew its fading claim on consumer app usage. But that's only if people buy the thing. As Jan Dawson, a telco analyst at Ovum, tells The New York Times, "There are lots of people who love Facebook, but I doubt if any of them feel like they need a more Facebook-centric experience on their phones. There isn't anything obviously missing." More. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001i_yYjQgN0dn8AezKtZSDq549oLd0Gc8UuCSG4LpacRDCPU5A_3fgghIDfP1z_ON6jjcCM6VyllWbn4CCM9r8Wyi7NMsOmrFQaeuIET9zDIdoGoZysWzxuOr9GwgYCHBgZYo1JJyOTc_GZRlsf8w-jot-uVo5VmxOjHTsvGHgDr9hGoQc7HO7MaUugOc9Q5NP3WA7zsycjBwziJi2B2qjK8MKzelL8V5SKydw_md1VNw=>

The Bottle And The Data Genie

 

In a piece on web privacy in the New York Times' Sunday edition, behavioral economist Alessandro Acquisti from Carnegie Mellon University tells the NYT in a series of anecdotes, studies and statements that consumers don't undestand whats happening with their data on the Web. Acquisti reasons, "I reveal my date of birth and hometown on my Facebook profile and an identity thief can reconstruct my Social Security number and steal my identity, or someone can send me 'happy birthday' messages on the day of my birthday, which makes me feel very good." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001LnCisKN9bPZh_GVgYEnBKuS9nIvSXuubgiXXdsMDg7v_FUpgbU8zIWDHenoF0SPHw3CDCEQnh6KZqXmTyXiVdR4h8tOKkH-31pgoo76ASvLjFtx4XJeE6_f7XBaCPbVT73JVknGQ7z-pTmHmPiMyyy7MHsklN-OYOyMFyI1udKH9ZQ05ctC0S5DArx_7q20oR1oGrRuGbAmUqFD19-VRHhcAUVsLvu5u> 

 

Mobile Insights

 

Venture Beat's Rakesh Agrawal called on four brands (Pandora, The Weather Channel, Sephora, Trulia) to weigh in on the mobile ad monetization challenge. "There are still too many buyers focused on clicks," Alex Linde, VP of digital and mobile apps at The Weather Channel, tells Agrawal. To uncover the "true ROI of mobile" Linde continues, agencies must connect all their metrics "across screens." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001LnCisKN9bPbb7lNqtr1bne5FqZbGBAoArkATRyR1UavC7zhdsy4upRG1sebypuQySHM2NfdCyJKhXvPE7rw16w37g-jRR7S482H4GvoSGs2f1Y96gSi34VWZENLoi6tgUhvHKRFT9Cf5SM7p5EYv7COh2JEgqdkOcFdaHWbSFwMRv5QWMSF445FqzicZG-aTaO1SH81AXK8LEhmKeDySPOIb--pQfGUZw_LC-LoagrQffcDvtt7Ctw==> .

 

Facebook+Android

 

Speculation is mounting as to what Facebook will unveil next week after inviting the press to "Come See Our New Home On Android." TechCrunch's Josh Constine notes that the "evidence aligns to say this is the Facebook Phone announcement people have been speculating about for years." Other rumors include a beefed up application layer and a Facebook-themed homescreen. More.  <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001LnCisKN9bPYIR6Qf8MhDflVrclkn5dujO-ejOpqbgvWdlQYtFQd7_QBby2psZNS8s42Dk9Dekx8Xjb87XxoibEwxdAdDcRDygF9PPqpXrlUSzlBsTFRQKDfiwCJyopqGb3rb7BUb08LN8sTMvOgGvHm0nZAf55jHbqxU2daGr8c=> 

 

Ad-Free Zones?

 

Selling ads for a small-to medium site isn't as easy as it seems, and some publishers are opting for simple paywalls and donations in lieu of ad support. AdAge's Matt Creamer does an informal survey that includes media news maven Jim Romenesko, who concedes that his work is now a "retirement hobby," and has relied on donations and Google AdSense. Others like Lisa Hickey, CEO of Good Men Media, which runs opinion pieces about the state of manhood, was disillusioned after hitting 1 million monthly uniques and seeing little return. "The CPMs slowly go down [on banner ads]," she says. "The number of ads we have to put on the site to break even goes up. It's a balancing act that doesn't get us to where we need to go." Read the rest <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001LnCisKN9bPZ291CXNX9cyEcxLj0IQgWLgoST2hIyNd9UhsJYR4WRxQTBCGZWm5PpmdU62ZsqesohO6VKvpWNrQLmwMLL9DUF9vIepA9K_0Qrmv3tv0juk224NQvnn4Om_mQcbGq_D6fJOzuyZsAX-QLE0VkIBisuV5yJXq6u_jVSLIwR49MwkfrSm6XDWD8Vzo6iQ-3oWI9l4TJ6aaylvQ==> .

 

Reddit Relevance

 

Reddit, that online volcano of meme-spewing activity, appears to be less and less of a digital trendsetter. PandoDaily's David Holmes, citing an academic study <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001LnCisKN9bPa6CBxZP8qczkU-wY69DYJCxQExK5hVUxvbemH7YnlGPgkWGx8Ka6mxkHQvQCbqaKdVa9Z2l-MOdGYbG-O35YEe603tyoozgXHEd3hkYrfr36XyBZ5ZffgZff2LPm0G1Z0LUilrFwLRoH7i6pFyFSUrp8dAVXlA-6c=>  that says more than half of Reddit's front page links have circulated elsewhere before, suggesting a burgeoning relevance problem. And it's something that should give social media marketers pause, as Holmes observes: "Unless you reward users for sharing content, they'll be nothing more than passive content consumers. And without engaging in your community, don't be surprised when they switch loyalties at the drop of a hat." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001LnCisKN9bPbQxSfZ3xE2dMf999SfHzU2DJlyCg_-cMtfV8Mk2q0n2HO9_ry914oc3SVsp-W5Y_nuzQDlBM8sIz7hixRQJHXKfqn36_F6xtTDthg_6rmC6vz8dxZmKiZvBLnd97OqhYWZYOTJZGz7S2_PagT9w3x6> .

DMP Gets Loan

 

Data management platform Lotame has perhaps decided it doesn't want to give away any more equity - at least, for now. The company has entered into a "venture loan" agreement with Horizon Technology Finance for a $5.5 million loan. According to the release, "Lotame plans to strengthen global initiatives across five continents, and make key hiring decisions to expand the sales, technology, and executive teams." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001LnCisKN9bPa3O_mMiGMSI_bNWcZ3D9TvY7BCw34yURY8MXJTb6O5b_HyuvT-vWGOeFIeVlWvN_ZVfU8kR3PZvu7XIwBt_40dRbRgDJVTXd_t3hJaopLpNPSi_-wNMTM7vmBANDvc4lRS422FF71QYCtM4hvOrBrAOqxr4-Fh3xJhDa7Sei7ROpz3h6eYP9Dj>  A bridge to the next round of financing or to being acquired by some unnamed company down the road?
